The Disliked Manner of Draping the Garment in Prayer
Explaining the disliked manner of draping the garment on one shoulder.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for placing the garment under one armpit during prayer and explain why it is disliked.

Core Idea
Covering both shoulders in prayer is mustahabb, so unnecessarily leaving one uncovered is makruh tanzihi.

In prayer, the manner of wearing one's garment can affect the completeness of the act. The Hanafi school specifies that while covering the shoulders is not obligatory, it is a recommended practice (mustahabb). Therefore, intentionally leaving a shoulder uncovered without a valid reason is considered mildly disliked (makruh tanzihi). This ruling stems from the general emphasis on proper adornment in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing the garment under the right armpit and throwing both ends over the left shoulder (or its opposite). The ruling is makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked).
The ruling applies explicitly to this specific manner.
2
Identify the reason (ta'lil)
The reason given in the text is that covering both shoulders is mustahabb (recommended) in prayer. Leaving a shoulder uncovered unnecessarily goes against this recommendation.
The Arabic phrase 'لأن ستر المنكبين مستحب' provides the cause.
3
Understand the category of dislike
Makruh tanzihi is the lightest level of dislike. It means the act is discouraged but not sinful; the prayer remains valid.
This is distinct from makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), which is closer to haram.
4
Contrast with other schools
In the Shafi'i school, covering the shoulders is considered part of the awrah (nakedness) for men, making it obligatory. Thus, exposing a shoulder would invalidate the prayer if done intentionally. Hanafis do not hold this view.
This difference is a practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of varying definitions of awrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يكره (جعل الثوب تحت إبطه الأيمن وطرح جانبيه على عاتقه الأيسر أو عكسه لأنّ ستر المنكبين مستحب في الصلاة فیکره ترکه تنزيهاً بغير ضرورة
And it is disliked to place the garment under his right armpit and throw its two ends over his left shoulder, or the opposite, because covering the shoulders is recommended in prayer, so leaving it is disliked tanzihan without necessity.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This is a ruling statement giving the reason. The disliked action is draping the garment in a way that leaves one shoulder uncovered, such as putting the garment under one armpit and throwing both ends over the opposite shoulder. The reason (ta'lil) is that covering both shoulders is mustahabb (recommended) in prayer, and leaving one shoulder uncovered unnecessarily is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). This is a Hanafi position; other schools may require covering both shoulders as a condition, but Hanafis consider it only recommended.

Key Terms
المنكب (al-mankab): Shoulder, specifically the area between the upper arm and neck
مكروه تنزيهي (makruh tanzihi): A disliked action that is not sinful, but leaving it is better; the act remains valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It leaves one shoulder uncovered unnecessarily
C) It is an act of arrogance
D) It is a waste of cloth

Key Takeaway
Covering both shoulders in prayer is mustahabb, and unnecessarily leaving one uncovered is makruh tanzihi.

Dislike of Lengthening First Rak'ah in Nafl
Hanafi disagreement on lengthening the first rak'ah in supererogatory prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl prayers and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl is disliked except for proven practices – the dispute turns on nafl's flexibility.

This short passage from Maraqi al-Falah and its hashaya reveals a subtle disagreement within the Hanafi school: is it makruh to elongate the first rak'ah in supererogatory prayers? The answer depends on whether one treats nafl as strictly analogous to fard or grants it greater leniency. Let's unpack the positions.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify what the matn (base text) declares: it is disliked (makruh) to lengthen the first rak'ah in every two-rak'ah unit (shaf') of nafl prayer.
Note the exception: unless the recitation is narrated from the Prophet or a Companion.
2
Identify the dissenting view
Imam Abu al-Yusr (and Imam Muhammad according to the sharh) holds it is not disliked. Understand their reasoning: nafl is inherently more flexible than fard.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the majority and a minority within the school.
3
Compare the proofs
The majority rely on analogy with fard and the principle that nafl follows fard unless specified otherwise. The dissenters argue that ease is the default for nafl, citing witr practice as precedent.
The exception for narrated practices shows that the default is dislike; the dissenters see the exception as proof of flexibility.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates the relied-upon position is the majority view (dislike). The commentary notes the differing opinion without overturning the base ruling.
For fatwa, the default is to consider it makruh tanzihi unless a specific narration supports the recitation.
5
Note the practical consequence
If you lead a nafl prayer and lengthen the first rak'ah, the prayer is valid but may be makruh. To avoid dislike, balance the rak'ahs or use a specific narrated recitation.
This applies to both individual and congregational nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يكره (إطالة) الركعة الأولى في كل شفع من (التطوع) إلا أن يكون مروياً عن النبي أو مأثوراً عن صحابي كقراءة سبح، وقل يا أيها الكافرون وقل الله أحد في الوتر فإنه من حيث القراءة ملحق بالنوافل، وقال الإمام أبو اليسر لا يكره لأن النوافل أمرها أسهل من الفرض
And it is disliked to lengthen the first rak'ah in every pair of nafl prayer, unless it is narrated from the Prophet or reported from a Companion, like reciting Subh, Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun, and Qul Allahu ahad in witr, for it is attached to nawafil in terms of recitation. Imam Abu al-Yusr said it is not disliked because nawafil are easier than fard.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The base text from Maraqi al-Falah states that lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl prayers is disliked, with exceptions for established practices like specific surahs in witr. However, the commentator reports that Imam Abu al-Yusr (and Imam Muhammad according to the sharh) holds it is not disliked, as nafl prayers are more flexible. The dispute hinges on whether nafl should be treated like fard in this regard. The mufta bihi position (according to the text's indication from the sharh) is that it is disliked according to the majority, but the opposite is also transmitted.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs, especially in nafl prayers which are performed in two-rak'ah units

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu al-Yusr, why is lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl not disliked?
A) Because the Prophet did it
B) Because nafl prayers are easier and more flexible
C) Because it is a sunnah
D) Because the Companions agreed on it

Key Takeaway
The default ruling for lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl is makruh tanzihi according to the majority, unless a specific narration supports it.

Dislike of Lengthening the Second Rak'ah by Three or More Verses
Ruling on making the second rak'ah longer than the first in all prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on making the second rak'ah longer than the first, identify the threshold of three verses, and apply the exception of tawsi'a.

Core Idea
Making the second rak'ah longer than the first by three or more verses is disliked, unless a specific Sunnah allowance exists.

In prayer, the Sunnah is for the first rak'ah to be longer than the second. This lesson clarifies when lengthening the second rak'ah becomes disliked, and distinguishes the rule for the third rak'ah. The ruling applies to both fard and nafl prayers by the most correct view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Lengthening the second rak'ah over the first by three or more verses is makruh tanzihi (disliked).
The dislike is not absolute; it depends on the threshold.
2
Note the threshold
The dislike only applies when the difference is three or more verses; less than that is not disliked.
3
Recognize the scope
This applies to all prayers: fard (by agreement) and nafl (by the stronger view, by analogy to fard).
4
Identify the exception
If a specific allowance (tawsi'a) is reported in the Sunnah, the lengthening is not disliked.
5
Distinguish the third rak'ah
Lengthening the third rak'ah is not disliked because it is considered the beginning of a new nafl prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يكره (تطويل) الركعة الثانية على الركعة (الأولى) بثلاث آيات فأكثر لا تطويل الثالثة لأنه ابتداء صلاة نفل (في جميع الصلوات) الفرض بالإتفاق، والنفل على الأصح إلحاقاً له بالفرض فيما لم يرد فيه تخصيص من التوسعة
And it is disliked to lengthen the second rak'ah over the first by three or more verses, not the lengthening of the third because it is the beginning of a nafl prayer. This applies in all prayers: in fard by agreement, and in nafl according to the most correct view, by analogy to fard in matters where no specific allowance is reported.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This ruling states that it is disliked to make the second rak'ah significantly longer than the first by three or more verses. This applies to both fard and nafl prayers. The reason is that the default Sunnah is to have the first rak'ah longer. The exception is when a specific allowance is reported (e.g., the Prophet lengthened the second rak'ah in some prayers). The ruling on the third rak'ah is different: since it begins a new set of nafl (in prayers like maghrib or witr), lengthening it is not disliked by the same rule.

Key Terms
التوسعة (al-tawsi'a): Specific reported allowance from the Sunnah to lengthen the second rak'ah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the threshold for the second rak'ah being longer than the first to be disliked?
A) One verse
B) Two verses
C) Three or more verses
D) Any difference

Key Takeaway
Lengthening the second rak'ah over the first by three or more verses is disliked in all prayers, except when a Sunnah allowance is reported.

Dislike of Repeating a Surah in Fard Prayer
Ruling on repeating surah in fard with exception and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on repeating a surah in fard prayer and identify the exceptions and conditions that change the ruling.

Core Idea
Repeating a surah in fard is disliked unless you know no other surah; in nafl it's fine.

This lesson examines a common question about recitation in prayer: is it allowed to repeat the same surah twice? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the type of prayer and the worshipper's knowledge of other surahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the same surah twice in one rak'ah or in two rak'ahs of a fard prayer. The ruling is that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked).
Dislike does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Note the exception for ignorance
If the worshipper does not know any other surah, repeating is not disliked but obligatory (wajib) because adding a surah after al-Fatihah is wajib in fard.
This exception only applies if the worshipper has not memorized another surah.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is the hadith: 'If you begin a surah, recite it in its proper order.' Deliberate repetition breaks the proper order and is therefore disliked.
The hadith is ahad, so its evidence is zanni.
4
Distinguish fard from nafl
In nafl prayer, repetition is not disliked because of its expansive nature, supported by the Prophet's practice of repeating a single verse in tahajjud and the practice of the Salaf.
This shows that the ruling is specific to fard prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكره (تكرار السورة في ركعة واحدة من (الفرض وكذا تكرارها في الركعتين إن حفظ غيرها، وتعمده لعدم وروده، فإن لم يحفظه وجب قراءتها لوجوب ضم السورة للفاتحة وإن نسي لا يترك لقوله : إن افتتحت سورة فاقرأها على نحوها وقيد بالفرض لأنه لا يكره التكرار في النفل لأن شأنه أوسع لأنه الله قام إلى الصباح بآية واحدة يكررها في تهجده وجماعة من السلف كانوا يحيون ليلتهم بآية العذاب أو الرحمة أو الرجاء أو الخوف
It is disliked to repeat a surah in one rak'ah of fard, and similarly to repeat it in two rak'ahs if he knows another surah. Deliberate repetition is disliked because it is not reported. If he does not memorize another, he must read it because adding a surah to al-Fatihah is obligatory. If he forgets, he does not leave it due to the saying: 'If you begin a surah, recite it in its proper order.' It is restricted to fard because repetition is not disliked in nafl, for its nature is expansive: indeed, Allah's Messenger stood until morning with a single verse repeating it in his tahajjud, and a group of the Salaf would spend their night with a verse of punishment or mercy or hope or fear.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This ruling covers the disliked nature of repeating the same surah in fard prayer, whether in the same rak'ah or in the two rak'ahs if one knows alternatives. The key exception is that if a person only knows one surah, they must repeat it because adding a surah to al-Fatihah is wajib. The proof is the hadith 'If you begin a surah, recite it in its proper order' (i.e., do not interrupt it). In nafl, repetition is not disliked because of the greater flexibility, as shown by the Prophet's practice of repeating a single verse in tahajjud.

Key Terms
تكرير السورة (takrir al-surah): Reciting the same surah twice in one rak'ah or in two rak'ahs of the same prayer
مكروه تنزيهاً (makruh tanzihan): A disliked act that is not sinful but should be avoided; the prayer remains valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When you want to
B) When you do not know any other surah to recite
C) When you are in a hurry
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Repeating a surah in fard is disliked unless you know no other surah; in nafl it's not disliked.

Disliking Repetition of a Surah in One Rak'ah of Fard
Ruling on repeating a surah in fard prayer with evidence and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating a surah in fard prayer and identify the specific conditions that change the ruling from disliked to obligatory.

Core Idea
Repeating a surah in fard prayer is disliked (makruh tanzihi) — but if you know no other, it becomes wajib.

In this passage from Maraqi al-Falah, the author addresses a common question: is it permissible to recite the same surah twice in one fard prayer? The ruling depends on whether the worshipper knows another surah. The text also provides the evidence and distinguishes fard from nafl prayers, clarifying that repetition in nafl is not disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the basic ruling
The act is repeating the same surah in one rak'ah or across two rak'ahs of a fard prayer. The basic ruling is that it is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
The karahah is tanzihiyyah, meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.
2
Identify the exception to the ruling
If the person does not know any other surah besides the one being repeated, then repetition is obligatory (wajib), not disliked. This is because joining a surah to al-Fatihah is wajib.
The text states: 'if he does not know, it is obligatory to read it'.
3
Understand the evidence (dalil)
The proof is a hadith: 'If you open a surah, recite it upon its pattern.' This command indicates that if one begins a surah, he should complete it without switching. The Hanafis use this to support the ruling of dislike for intentional repetition, but also to allow continuing the same surah if one forgets.
The hadith is ahad, so its proof is zanni, leading to karahah tanzihiyyah rather than tahrim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكره (تكرار السورة في ركعة واحدة من (الفرض وكذا تكرارها في الركعتين إن حفظ غيرها، وتعمده لعدم وروده، فإن لم يحفظه وجب قراءتها لوجوب ضم السورة للفاتحة وإن نسي لا يترك لقوله : إن افتتحت سورة فاقرأها على نحوها وقيد بالفرض لأنه لا يكره التكرار في النفل لأن شأنه أوسع لأنه الله قام إلى الصباح بآية واحدة يكررها في تهجده وجماعة من السلف كانوا يحيون ليلتهم بآية العذاب أو الرحمة أو الرجاء أو الخوف قوله : ( في ركعة واحدة) وكذا في الركعتين كما في النهر عن القنية، وأما ما ورد أنه قرأ في أولى المغرب إذا زلزلت وأعادها في الثانية فيحمل على بيان الجواز والكراهة تنزيهية أفاده السيد. قوله : (وإن نسي لا يترك) فرضه المؤلف هنا في الركعة الواحدة، وفي الشرح في الركعة الثانية بأن أراد سورة غير ما قرأ أولاً فقرأها بعينها فإنه لا يترك للحديث. قوله : (على نحوها أي قصدها أي قصدك إياه ولا تغيرها.
It is disliked to repeat a surah in one rak'ah of fard, and likewise repeating it in two rak'ahs if he knows another surah, and his intention [to repeat] is due to its not occurring [to him]. If he does not know [another surah], it is obligatory to read it because it is obligatory to join a surah to al-Fatihah. And if he forgets, he does not leave it due to his statement: 'If you open a surah, then recite it upon its pattern.' And it is restricted to fard because repetition is not disliked in nafl, because its matter is broader because Allah stood until morning with one verse repeating it in his tahajjud, and a group of predecessors used to spend their night with a verse of punishment, mercy, hope, or fear. His statement: 'in one rak'ah' and likewise in two rak'ahs as in al-Nahr from al-Qunyah. And as for what is reported that he recited in the first of Maghrib 'Idha zulzilat' and repeated it in the second, it is interpreted as indicating permissibility, and the dislike is tanzihi, as stated by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'and if he forgets, he does not leave it' the author posited it here in one rak'ah, and in al-Sharh in the second rak'ah: that he intended a surah other than what he read first but read the same one, then he does not leave it due to the hadith. His statement: 'upon its pattern' meaning his intention, i.e., your intention for it and do not change it.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on repeating a surah in fard prayer. It states that it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) to repeat the same surah in one rak'ah or in two rak'ahs if one knows another surah. However, if one does not know any other surah, repeating is obligatory because joining a surah to al-Fatihah is mandatory. The proof is a hadith commanding to recite a surah upon its pattern. The dislike is specific to fard; in nafl, repetition is not disliked because the Prophet and the Salaf practiced it. The commentator clarifies that the hadith about repeating a surah in Maghrib indicates permissibility, and the dislike is tanzihi, not tahrimi.

Key Terms
تكرار (takrār): Repeating the same surah within a single rak'ah or across two rak'ahs.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karāhah al-tanzīhiyyah): A level of dislike that is not sinful but better avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible without dislike
B) Disliked (makruh tanzihi)
C) Obligatory to repeat
D) Invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
Repeating a surah in fard prayer is disliked but not prohibited; it becomes obligatory only when one knows no other surah.

Reciting Surahs Out of Order in Prayer: Fard vs Nafl
Ruling on reading a surah earlier in the Quran than one already recited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reading a surah earlier than one already recited in obligatory and supererogatory prayers, explain the reason for the difference, and apply the ruling to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Reading the Quran in reverse order is disliked in fard but not in nafl prayers.

This passage from Maraqi al-Falah addresses a common question: what is the ruling if a worshipper reads a surah earlier in the Quran after already reciting a later one? The answer is not uniform; it depends on whether the prayer is obligatory or voluntary. The text also provides guidance for accidental recitation to avoid a greater disliked act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reading a surah that appears earlier in the Quran than the one already recited (e.g., reciting al-Ikhlas after al-Nas). In fard prayers, this is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked). In nafl prayers, it is not disliked according to the relied-upon view.
The text uses 'above' to mean earlier in the standard order.
2
Examine the evidence
The proof includes Ibn Mas'ud's statement: 'Whoever reads the Quran upside down is himself upside down.' This indicates that maintaining the Quranic order is a duty of recitation. However, the scope of supererogatory prayers is broader, so the exception is justified.
The dalil is a statement of a Companion, considered a hadith in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the exception for nafl
Authorities like al-Ashbah, al-Ghazzi, and al-Hamawi explicitly exempt supererogatory prayers. The opposing view (some virtuous scholars) holds that the dislike extends to nafl because order is a duty, but the majority rejects this due to the expansive nature of nafl.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school over the application in nafl.
4
Apply to accidental recitation
If one unintentionally recites a late surah (e.g., Surat al-Nas) in the first rak'ah of fard, the better option is to repeat the same surah in the second rak'ah rather than recite an earlier one. This avoids the greater dislike of reading upside down.
Repetition is considered less severe than reversing the order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (قراءة سورة فوق التي قرأها قال ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه من قرأ القرآن منكوساً فهو منكوس وما شرع لتعليم الأطفال إلا ليتيسر الحفظ بقصر السور وإذا قرأ في الأولى قل أعوذ برب الناس لا عن قصد يكررها في الثانية، ولا كراهة فيه حذراً عن كراهة القراءة منكوساً، ولو ختم القرآن في الأولى يقرأ من البقرة في الثانية لقوله : (خير الناس الحال المرتحل» يعني الخاتم المفتتح قوله : (ويكره قراءة سورة) وكذا الآية فوق الآية مطلقاً سواء كان في ركعتين أو ركعة، واستثنى في الأشباه النافلة فلا يكره فيها ذلك، وأقره عليه الغزي والحموي ونقله عن أبي اليسر وجزم به في البحر، والدرر وغيرهما. وقال بعض الفضلاء، وفيه تأمل لأن النكس إذا كره خارج الصلاة كما يرشد إليه قوله : وما شرع لتعليم الأطفال الخ لكون الترتيب من واجبات التلاوة ففي النافلة أولى وكون باب النفل واسعاً لا يستلزم العموم، بل في بعض الأحكام .اهـ. قوله : (لا . قصد) أما عن إذا قرأها عن قصد فيكره، ولكن يقرؤها في الثانية أيضاً، ولا يقرأ من فوقها، قال البزازي لأن التكرار أهون من القراءة منكوساً كما في تنوير البصائر. قوله : لقوله ) أي فقلنا بأنه يبتدىء القرآن، ويختم ويبتدىء أيضاً مرة أخرى، ويختم ليحصل تلك الفضيلة، قوله: (وقال بعضهم: لا يكره إذا كانت السورة طويلة لأنها بمنزلة سورتين قصيرتين بحر قوله : (كما لو كان بينهما سورتان قصيرتان) هو الأصح كذا في الدرة المنيفة. قوله : (والجمع بين سورتين الخ) أي في ركعة واحدة لما فيه من شبهة التفضيل والهجر. قوله : (لا يكره هذا في النفل) يعني القراءة منكوساً، والفصل والجمع كما . هو مفاد عبارة الخلاصة حيث قال بعد ما ذكر المسائل الثلاث وهذا كله في الفرائض أما في النوافل لا يكره اهـ وفيها لو كبر للركوع، ثم بدا له أن يزيد في القراءة لا بأس به مالم يركع .اهـ.
It is disliked to read a surah above the one he read (i.e., earlier in the Quran). Ibn Mas'ud said: 'Whoever reads the Quran upside down is himself upside down.' And it was only prescribed for teaching children to facilitate memorization by short surahs. If he reads in the first [rak'ah] 'Qul a'udhu bi rabbi al-nas' unintentionally, he repeats it in the second, and there is no dislike in that out of caution against the dislike of reading upside down. And if he completed the Quran in the first rak'ah, he reads from al-Baqarah in the second due to his statement: 'The best of people are the one who starts and departs,' meaning the one who completes and then starts anew. His statement: 'It is disliked to read a surah above a surah'—similarly a verse above a verse absolutely, whether in two rak'ahs or one. Al-Ashbah exempts supererogatory prayers, so it is not disliked there; al-Ghazzi and al-Hamawi agreed, and it is narrated from Abu al-Yusr, and confirmed in al-Bahr, al-Durar, etc. Some virtuous scholars said there is reflection, because if reading upside down is disliked outside prayer, as indicated by his statement 'It was only prescribed for teaching children...' because order is one of the duties of recitation, then in supererogatory prayers it is more appropriate [to still dislike], and the fact that the scope of supererogatory is broad does not necessitate generality, but only in some rulings. His statement: 'not intentionally'—if he reads it intentionally, it is disliked, but he still reads it in the second rak'ah and does not read a surah above it. Al-Bazzazi said: 'Because repetition is less severe than reading upside down.' His statement: 'due to his statement' means we say he begins the Quran, completes it, and then begins again to attain that virtue. His statement: 'And some said: it is not disliked if the surah is long, because it is like two short surahs.' [Al-Bahr said:] 'The correct view is that if there are two short surahs between them.' His statement: 'And combining two surahs...' means in one rak'ah, due to [the appearance] of preference and abandonment. His statement: 'This is not disliked in supererogatory prayers' means reading upside down, separating, and combining, as is the purport of the expression in al-Khulasah, where he said after mentioning the three issues: 'All this is in obligatory prayers; as for supererogatory prayers, it is not disliked.' And in it: if he said the takbir for bowing, then it occurs to him to add to the recitation, there is no harm in it as long as he has not bowed.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of reciting a surah in a non-Quranic order (i.e., reading a surah that appears earlier in the Quran after having recited a later one). It is disliked in obligatory prayers but not in supererogatory ones, according to the relied-upon view. The proof includes the statement of Ibn Mas'ud that such recitation is 'upside down.' The commentator explains that if one accidentally reads a surah from the end of the Quran in the first rak'ah, it is better to repeat the same surah in the second rak'ah rather than read an earlier surah, to avoid the greater dislike of reading upside down. There is a difference of opinion among later scholars regarding supererogatory prayers; some argue that since reciting in order is a duty of tilawah, it should still be disliked, but the majority exempt nafl. The passage also discusses the practice of completing the Quran and starting again, which is recommended.

Key Terms
منكوساً (mankūsan): Reading the Quran in reverse order (later surahs before earlier ones).
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person accidentally reads Surat al-Nas in the first rak'ah of fard prayer, what should he do in the second rak'ah to avoid a greater disliked act?
A) Read a surah from the beginning of the Quran
B) Repeat Surat al-Nas
C) Read a medium-length surah
D) Skip the surah and only recite al-Fatihah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, reading the Quran in reverse order is disliked in obligatory prayers but not in supererogatory prayers, and accidental repetition is preferred over changing the order.

Disliking Separating with a Surah Between Two Surahs
Ruling on inserting a surah between two surahs read in two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inserting a surah between two surahs read in two rak'ahs, explain the underlying reason (shubhat al-tafdil), and apply the exception for supererogatory prayers.

Core Idea
Inserting a surah between two surahs in fard salah is disliked, but not in nafl.

In the prayer, the recitation of surahs follows certain etiquettes. This lesson examines a specific act: separating between two surahs recited in two rak'ahs by inserting another surah. The Hanafi school considers this disliked in obligatory prayers due to the appearance of preference and abandonment. However, the ruling differs for supererogatory prayers, and there is a nuance regarding long surahs. We will explore the reasoning and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is 'separating with a surah between two surahs read in two rak'ahs' — meaning, in the first rak'ah you read a surah, in the second you read a different surah, but before that you recite a third surah as a separator. The ruling is makruh (disliked) in fard prayers.
The dislike applies whether the separator is a full surah or a verse.
2
Understand the Reason (Illah)
The reason given is 'shubhat al-tafdil wa al-hajr' — it appears as if you are preferring one surah over another or abandoning a previously intended surah. This leads to the dislike.
This illah is derived from the principle of avoiding any resemblance to innovation or disrespect.
3
Note the Intra-Madhhab Difference
Some Hanafi scholars said it is not disliked if the inserted surah is long (e.g., equivalent to two short surahs). However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it remains disliked.
The difference is based on how strongly the appearance of preference is perceived.
4
Distinguish Fard vs. Nafl
All the above (dislike for separating, combining two surahs in one rak'ah, reading upside down) apply only to fard prayers. In nafl (supererogatory) prayers, these actions are not disliked.
This follows the general leniency in nafl acts.
5
Apply the Ruling to Similar Cases
The passage also mentions that combining two surahs in one rak'ah (al-jam‘ bayn sūratayn) is similarly disliked in fard. Also, if one has said the takbir for bowing and then wants to add more recitation, it is permissible as long as he has not actually bowed.
These additional rulings reinforce the principle of avoiding unnecessary innovation in fard prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (فصله بسورة بين سورتين قرأهما في ركعتين) لما فيه من شبهة التفضيل والهجر وقال بعضهم : لا يكره إذا كانت السورة طويلة كما لو كان بينهما سورتان قصيرتان ويكره الانتقال لآية من سورتها، ولو فصل بآية والجمع بين سورتين بينهما سور أو سورة في الخلاصة لا يكره هذا في النفل قوله : (والجمع بين سورتين الخ) أي في ركعة واحدة لما فيه من شبهة التفضيل والهجر. قوله : (لا يكره هذا في النفل) يعني القراءة منكوساً، والفصل والجمع كما . هو مفاد عبارة الخلاصة حيث قال بعد ما ذكر المسائل الثلاث وهذا كله في الفرائض أما في النوافل لا يكره اهـ وفيها لو كبر للركوع، ثم بدا له أن يزيد في القراءة لا بأس به مالم يركع .اهـ.
It is disliked to separate with a surah between two surahs that he read in two rak'ahs, because of the resemblance of preference and abandonment. And some said: it is not disliked if the surah is long, as if there were two short surahs between them. And it is disliked to go to a verse from its surah. And if he separates with a verse, and the combining of two surahs with a surah or one surah between them in al-Khulasah, this is not disliked in supererogatory prayers. His statement: 'And combining two surahs...' means in one rak'ah, due to the resemblance of preference and abandonment. His statement: 'This is not disliked in supererogatory' means reading upside down, separating, and combining, as is the purport of the expression in al-Khulasah, where he said after mentioning the three issues: 'All this is in obligatory prayers; as for supererogatory prayers, it is not disliked.' And in it: if he said the takbir for bowing, then it occurs to him to add to the recitation, there is no harm in it as long as he has not bowed.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on separating between two surahs recited in two rak'ahs by inserting a different surah. It is disliked in obligatory prayers because it may give the appearance of preferring one surah over another or abandoning a previously intended surah. However, some scholars say it is not disliked if the inserted surah is long, equivalent to two short surahs. The ruling applies to separating with a verse as well. Combining two surahs in one rak'ah is also disliked. All these dislikes apply only to obligatory prayers; in supererogatory prayers, they are not disliked. The passage also notes that if one has already said the takbir for bowing and then wishes to add more recitation, it is permissible as long as he has not actually bowed.

Key Terms
الفصل بسورة (al-faṣl bi sūrah): Inserting a different surah between two surahs read in two rak'ahs.
الجمع بين سورتين (al-jam‘ bayn sūratayn): Reading two surahs in one rak'ah.
شبهة التفضيل والهجر (shubhat al-tafdīl wa al-hajr): The resemblance of preferring one surah over another or abandoning a surah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is disliked
B) No, it is recommended
C) It is forbidden
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, inserting a surah between two surahs or combining two surahs in one rak'ah is disliked in fard prayers but not in nafl, based on the illah of shubhat al-tafdil wa al-hajr.

Ruling on Intentionally Smelling Perfume During Prayer
Ruling on smelling perfume in prayer with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentionally smelling perfume in prayer, distinguish between intentional and unintentional cases, and explain when it may invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Intentional smelling of perfume during prayer is disliked; active handling may invalidate.

In this lesson, we examine a specific rule from salah: what happens if a worshiper intentionally smells perfume? The text distinguishes between passive inhalation and active handling, and clarifies the degree of dislike and potential invalidation based on the actions involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and baseline ruling
Determine what the ruling is on intentionally smelling perfume during prayer. The text states it is disliked (makruh).
The hadith or analogical basis is that it is not from the actions of prayer.
2
Note the condition of intentionality
The dislike only applies when the person intentionally seeks the scent. If it enters the nose without intention, there is no dislike.
Intentionality (qasd) is key.
3
Analyze the sub-case of active handling
If the person actively holds a fragrant object (e.g., a rose) to the nose and smells it, some Hanafi authorities say the prayer is invalidated because it gives the appearance of being outside prayer. Others limit invalidation to cases of excessive movement.
The ruling depends on the amount of action and the perception of bystanders.
4
Compare different Hanafi opinions
The text notes a difference: some commentators from al-Munyah hold that it does not invalidate unless it involves excessive motion. Recognize that this is a later Hanafi refinement.
This shows an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (شم طيب) قصداً لأنه ليس من فعل الصلاة قوله : (قصداً) أما لو دخلت الرائحة أنفه بغير قصد فلا كذا في الشرح . قوله : ويكره شم (طيب) كأن يدلك موضع سجوده بطيب، أو يضع ذا رائحة طيبة عند أنفه في موضع السجود ليستنشقه أما إذا أمسكه بيده، وشمه فالظاهر الفساد لأن من راه يجزم زم أنه في غير الصلاة، وأفاد بعض شراح المنية أنها لا تفسد بذلك أي إذا لم يكن بعمل كثير .
It is disliked to smell perfume intentionally, because it is not from the actions of prayer. His statement: 'intentionally' – if the scent enters his nose unintentionally, then it is not [disliked] as in al-Sharh. His statement: 'It is disliked to smell perfume' such as rubbing his prostration place with perfume, or placing a fragrant thing near his nose in the prostration place to inhale it. But if he holds it in his hand and smells it, the apparent is that it invalidates [the prayer], because one who sees him will be certain that he is not in prayer. And some commentators of al-Munyah state that it does not invalidate by that, i.e., if it is not a lot of action.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on smelling perfume during prayer. It is disliked (makruh) if done intentionally, because it is not part of the prayer. If the scent enters the nose without intention, there is no dislike. However, if one physically holds a fragrant object and smells it, according to some scholars this invalidates the prayer because it gives the appearance of being outside prayer. Other scholars say it does not invalidate unless it involves excessive movement. The distinction depends on the amount of action involved.

Key Terms
شم الطيب (shamm al-ṭīb): Intentionally inhaling the smell of perfume during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Invalidates the prayer
D) Obligatory to repeat the prayer

Key Takeaway
Intentional smelling of perfume in prayer is disliked; active handling may invalidate depending on the extent of movement, with the later Hanafi position favoring leniency for minimal actions.

Disliking Fanning Oneself in Prayer
Ruling on fanning oneself with a garment or fan during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fanning during prayer and distinguish between fanning with a garment and fanning with a fan.

Core Idea
Fanning with a fan invalidates prayer; fanning with a garment is only disliked.

During prayer, maintaining humility (khushu') is essential. Any action that disrupts concentration is discouraged. This lesson explores the specific ruling on fanning oneself, whether with a garment or a fan, and clarifies when a small action becomes impermissible based on the observer's perception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that it is disliked (yukrah) to fan oneself with a garment or a fan once or twice, because it contradicts khushu'.
The ruling is makruh tanzihi for the general case.
2
Distinguish between garment and fan
Fanning with the sleeve does not invalidate, but fanning with a fan (mihaffah) invalidates the prayer even if done once, because the observer is certain the person is not in prayer.
Key distinction: appearance to the observer.
3
Understand the concept of 'small action' vs 'large action'
The base text says fanning once or twice is a small action (qalil), but fanning with a fan is treated as invalidating regardless of repetition due to its nature.
The definition of 'large action' (kathir) is three movements; here fanning with fan is an exception.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Some earlier texts consider fanning with a fan merely disliked, but later authoritative works (al-Dhakhirah, al-Muhit, al-Hindiyyah) say it invalidates.
The mufta bihi is the invalidating view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (ترويحه) أي جلب الروح بفتح الراء نسيم الريح (بثوبه أو مروحة) بكسر الميم وفتح الواو (مرة أو مرتين لأنه ينافي الخشوع وإن كان عملاً قليلاً قوله : (بكسر الميم وفتح الواو) وأما بفتح الميم فهو المفازة ، والجمع المراويح وجمع الأولى المصنف. قوله : أو مرتين) هذا بناء منه على أن العمل الكثير ثلاث نقل عن كذا مراوح حركات، والقليل دون ذلك وقد علمت المعتمد، والذي في الذخيرة أنها تفسد بالمروحة وإن لم يتكرر بخلاف الكم، ونقله رضي الدين في المحيط عن المنتقي، ونصه تروح بطرف كمه لا تفسد، ولو تروح بالمروحة قالوا تفسد لأن الناظر إليه يتيقن انه ليس في الصلاة اهـ. فقد بنى الفرع على ما هو الصحيح في تعريف العمل الكثير، وفي الهندية عن التتارخانية يكره أن يذب بيده الذباب أو البعوض إلا عند الحاجة بعمل قليل اهـ .
It is disliked to fan himself (bringing wind), with his garment or a fan (mihaffah, with kasr on meem and fatha on waw), once or twice, because it contradicts humility, even if it is a small action. His statement: (with kasr on meem and fatha on waw) – with fatha on meem it means desert; the plural is marawih; the word is from the author. His statement: 'once or twice' – this is based on the principle that a lot of action is three movements, and a little is less than that, and you have known the relied-upon view. What is in al-Dhakhirah: it invalidates with a fan even if not repeated, unlike with the sleeve. Rudi al-Din in al-Muhit narrated from al-Muntaqa: 'Fanning with the tip of the sleeve does not invalidate, but if he fans with a fan, they said it invalidates because the observer will be certain that he is not in prayer.' So the ruling is based on what is correct in defining a lot of action. And in al-Hindiyyah from al-Tatarkhaniyyah: 'It is disliked to swat flies or mosquitoes with the hand except when necessary with a small action.'
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage discusses fanning oneself during prayer, whether with a garment or a fan. It is disliked (makruh) to do it once or twice because it goes against khushu' (humility). However, some scholars differentiate: fanning with a fan may invalidate the prayer even if done once, because it gives the appearance of being outside prayer. Fanning with the sleeve does not invalidate. The criterion is whether the action is considered 'a lot' of movement; according to some, three movements are a lot. The text also mentions that swatting flies or mosquitoes is only disliked when there is no need, and if needed, a small action is permissible.

Key Terms
الترويح (al-tarwīḥ): Fanning oneself to get air during prayer.
العمل الكثير (al-‘amal al-kathīr): A large amount of movement that invalidates prayer; typically three consecutive movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is true about fanning with a fan (mihaffah) during prayer?
A) It is always permissible.
B) It is disliked but does not invalidate.
C) It invalidates the prayer even if done once.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
Fanning with a fan invalidates prayer; fanning with a sleeve is merely disliked; always consider the observer's perception.

Disliking Moving Fingers or Toes Away from Qibla in Sujud
Ruling with proof: dislike of turning limbs from Qibla in sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on moving fingers or toes away from Qibla in sujud and identify its dalil and legal reasoning.

Core Idea
Moving fingers or toes from Qibla in sujud is disliked because it contradicts the sunnah of directing limbs to Qibla.

This passage addresses the etiquette of sujud: one's fingers and toes should ideally face the Qibla. Turning them away, even slightly, incurs dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah). This ruling is rooted in a prophetic directive to face the Qibla with as many limbs as possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is turning the fingers of the hands or feet away from the Qibla during sujud. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Let him direct from his limbs to the Qibla as much as he can' (فَلْيُوَجِّـهْ مِنْ أَعْضَائِهِ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ مَا اسْتَطَاعَ).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فَلْيُوَجِّـهْ' indicates a directive; turning the limbs away contradicts this directive, thus the act is disliked.
The hadith is ahad and zanni, so the directive does not reach the level of obligation.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf in interpretation
The commentator notes two meanings of 'away from Qibla': (1) general direction – disliked only if turned to east or west; (2) the exact point – even a slight turn is disliked to avoid disagreement.
5
Confirm the nature of dislike
The text explicitly says the dislike is tanzihi (not tahrimi), as it leaves a sunnah but does not invalidate prayer or incur sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (تحويل أصابع يديه أو رجليه عن القبلة في السجود) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم فليوجه من أعضائه إلى القبلة ما استطاع (و) في (غيره ) أي السجود لما فيه من إزالتها عن الموضع المسنون قوله : ( عن القبلة) انظر هل المراد عن جهتها فلا يكره إلا إذا وجه إلى المشارق أو المغارب أو المراد العين فيكره لتحويل اليسير خروجاً من الخلاف قوله : (ما استطاع إنما قال : ذلك لأن من | الأعضاء ما لا يمكن توجيهه أصلاً كالظهر وأعلى الشخص وأسفله». قوله : (لما فيه الخ) يفيد أن الكراهة تنزيهية كما ان قوله بعد ذلك لتركه السنة يفيد ذلك.
It is disliked to turn his fingers of hands or feet away from the Qibla in sujud, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Let him direct from his limbs to the Qibla as much as he can.' And in other (postures) besides sujud, because it removes them from the sunnah location. His statement: 'away from the Qibla' – consider whether it means away from its direction, so it is only disliked if he turns towards the east or west, or it means the specific point, so it is disliked even for a small turning to exit from the difference of opinion. His statement: 'as much as he can' – he said that because some limbs cannot be directed at all, like the back, the top of the person, and the bottom. His statement: 'because of what is in it etc.' indicates that the dislike is tanzihi, just as his later statement 'because he leaves the sunnah' indicates that.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on turning one's fingers or toes away from the Qibla during sujud. It is disliked because the hadith instructs directing as much as possible towards the Qibla. The commentator explains that the 'turning' could refer to direction (e.g., pointing to east/west) or the exact point; in the latter case, even a slight turn is disliked to avoid disagreement. The dislike is tanzihi, as it is leaving a sunnah. Similarly, in other postures, moving them from the sunnah position is disliked.

Key Terms
تحويل الأصابع (taḥwīl al-aṣābi‘): Turning fingers or toes away from Qibla during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Disliked Omissions of Hand Placements in Prayer
Rulings on omitting hand placements during different prayer positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four hand placements whose omission is disliked in prayer and explain why they are makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Leaving sunnah hand placements in prayer is makruh tanzihi, not invalidating.

In the Hanafi school, specific hand placements during various postures of prayer are considered sunnah. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi enumerates four such placements and clearly states that abandoning them is disliked (makruh tanzihi). Understanding these details helps you perfect your prayer without unnecessary rigidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four disliked omissions
List the four specific hand placements that, if omitted, incur dislike: (1) hands on knees in ruku', (2) hands on thighs between sajdahs, (3) hands on thighs during tashahhud, (4) right hand on left in qiyam.
The fourth is specifically during standing, which includes actual standing or sitting if unable.
2
Understand the ruling level
Recognize that omitting any of these is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not haram or invalidating. The text says 'because it abandons the sunnah'.
This is a clear example of a sunnah act whose omission is disliked but does not affect the validity of the prayer.
3
Examine the commentator's clarification
Note that the commentator extends 'standing' to include legal standing (e.g., sitting when unable to stand). This ensures the ruling applies to all valid postures.
This prevents the ruling from being too narrow.
4
Distinguish from wajib acts
Contrast these sunnah acts with wajib acts (like the first tashahhud). Omitting a wajib requires sujud al-sahw; omitting a sunnah does not.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (ترك وضع اليدين على الركبتين في الركوع وترك وضعهما على الفخذين فيما بين السجدتين، وفي حال التشهد، وترك وضع اليمين على اليسار حال القيام لتركه السنة) قوله : (حال القيام) الحقيقي، أو الحكمي كالقعود كذا في مجمع الأنهر .
It is disliked to abandon placing the hands on the knees in ruku', and to abandon placing them on the thighs between the two sajdahs, and in the state of tashahhud, and to abandon placing the right hand on the left in the state of standing, because it abandons the sunnah. His statement: 'state of standing' – real or legal standing, like sitting, as in Majma‘ al-Anhur.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage enumerates several actions whose omission is disliked in prayer: not placing hands on knees during ruku', not placing hands on thighs between sajdahs and during tashahhud, and not placing the right hand over the left during qiyam. The dislike is because these are sunnah acts; leaving them is makruh tanzihi but does not invalidate the prayer. The commentator notes that 'standing' includes both actual standing and legal standing (e.g., sitting in case of inability).

Key Terms
وضع اليدين (waḍ‘ al-yadayn): Placing the hands in specific positions during different postures of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Omitting any of the four specific hand placements in prayer (ruku', between sajdahs, tashahhud, qiyam) is makruh tanzihi because they are sunnah acts.

Yawning in Prayer: Ruling and Suppression Methods
Ruling on yawning in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on yawning in prayer and apply the recommended methods to suppress it.

Core Idea
Yawning in prayer is disliked; suppress it by biting your lip or using your hand/sleeve.

Yawning during prayer is considered disliked (makruh tanzihi) because it stems from laziness and contradicts the spirit of humility. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance on how to suppress a yawn when it overcomes you, distinguishing between permissible and impermissible ways of covering the mouth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that yawning (al-tatā'ub) during prayer is classed as makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). The text explicitly states 'يكره التثاؤب'.
The ruling is based on the act itself, not the intention.
2
Understand the reason for dislike
The reason given is that yawning comes from laziness (al-takassul) and fullness (al-imtilā'), which detract from khushū' (focus) in prayer.
Note: Fullness here refers to physical satiety, often leading to drowsiness.
3
Identify the recommended actions to suppress
If a yawn overcomes you, first try to suppress it by biting your lip. If that fails, use your hand or sleeve. The posture determines which hand: right hand (or sleeve) while standing, left hand in other positions.
The hand should be placed with the back (zahr) facing the mouth, not the palm.
4
Recognize the limit of covering
Covering the mouth with the hand is only permissible when necessary (li-darūra). If you can suppress by biting your lip, covering with the hand becomes disliked itself.
This is based on the commentator's note from al-Nahr and al-Khulāsa.
5
Cite the proof
The hadith 'Indeed Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning' (إن الله يحب العطاس ويكره التثاؤب) is the primary evidence. The explicit dislike in the text indicates karāha.
The hadith is narrated in Sahih Muslim; the chain is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (التثاؤب لأنه من التكاسل والامتلاء فإن غلبه فليكظم ما استطاع ولو بأخذ شفته بسته، وبوضع ظهر يمينه أو كمه في القيام ويساره في غيره لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : إن الله : يحب ... قوله : (وبوضع ظهر يمينه) هذا إنما يفعل إن لم يمكن منعه بأخذ الشفة لو غطى فمه بيده متمكناً من أخذ شقته كره نهر عن الخلاصة لأن التغطية مكروهة إلا لضرورة أفاده السيد قال في البحر وضع اليد ثابت في مسلم والكم قياس عليه كذا في الشرح قوله: (في القيام ويساره في غيره كذا في البحر وذكره العلامة التحريري، وقرره ولده
It is disliked to yawn because it is from laziness and fullness. If it overcomes him, let him suppress it as much as he can, even by taking his lip with his teeth, and by placing the back of his right hand or his sleeve during standing, and his left hand in other postures, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah loves...' His statement: 'and by placing the back of his right hand' – this is done only if he cannot prevent it by taking the lip. If he covers his mouth with his hand while being able to take his lip, it is disliked according to al-Nahr from al-Khulasah, because covering is disliked except for necessity, as stated by al-Sayyid. In al-Bahr: placing the hand is established in Muslim, and the sleeve is analogous to it as in al-Sharh. His statement: 'in standing and his left in other postures' as in al-Bahr, mentioned by al-Allamah al-Tahriri and confirmed by his son.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on yawning in prayer: it is disliked because it indicates laziness and fullness. To suppress a yawn, one should try to prevent it by biting the lip or placing the back of the right hand over the mouth during standing, and the left hand in other postures. However, if one can prevent it by biting the lip, covering the mouth with the hand is itself disliked because covering is only allowed due to necessity. The hadith (which reports that Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning) is cited as proof. The commentator notes that the hand placement is supported by Sahih Muslim, and using the sleeve is analogous.

Key Terms
التثاؤب (al-tatā'ub): Yawning, considered disliked in prayer due to laziness.
يَكْظِم (yakzim): To suppress or hold back (a yawn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended way to suppress a yawn during prayer if one cannot prevent it by biting the lip?
A) Place the back of the right hand over the mouth while standing
B) Use the left hand
C) Leave the prayer
D) Continue yawning

Key Takeaway
Yawning in prayer is disliked; suppress it first by biting the lip, then by using the hand or sleeve appropriately based on posture.

Disliked Actions in Prayer (Makruhat as-Salah) – A Comprehensive Overview
Listing disliked actions in prayer with legal proofs and commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major disliked actions in prayer according to the Hanafi school, state their legal classification (makruh tahrimi or makruh tanzihi), and explain the evidence from the Sunnah for each.

Core Idea
Preserving khushu‘ is the foundation; actions that undermine it, even small, are disliked, and some are prohibitively disliked when associated with the devil.

This lesson surveys the actions that are disliked (makruh) during prayer, as enumerated in the Hanafi text Hashiya al-Tahtawi. The common thread is that these actions either contradict the required state of khushu‘ (focus and humility) or deviate from the sunna postures. We will examine each ruling, its proof, and the nuances in degree (tahrimi vs. tanzihi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the action
Pinpoint the exact behavior being ruled as makruh (e.g., fanning, yawning, closing eyes).
2
Determine the degree of dislike
Classify as makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked, close to haram) or makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). Check the evidence for the ruling.
The text uses 'يكره' for most, but the commentary specifies tahrimi for yawning based on the hadith.
3
Locate the evidence (dalil)
Identify the proof cited – usually a hadith or the principle of khushu‘. For yawning, the hadith is explicit; for others, it may be implicit.
4
Note exceptional circumstances
Check if there is any condition that removes the dislike (e.g., closing eyes for a benefit like avoiding distractions).
The text says 'except for a benefit' for closing eyes.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Use a real-life example to confirm understanding of the ruling and its practical implication.

(من التكاسل)
The Book of Prayer. It is not from the actions of prayer (and) it is disliked (to fan oneself), meaning bringing air by opening the ra' (wind breeze) (with his garment or a fan) with kasr of the meem and fatha of the waw (once or twice) because it contradicts khushu', even if it is a small action. (And) it is disliked (to turn the fingers of his hands or feet from the qibla in prostration) due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Let him direct from his limbs toward the qibla as much as he is able.' (And) in (other than) i.e. prostration, because it removes them from the sunna position. (And) it is disliked (to leave placing the hands on the knees in bowing, and to leave placing them on the thighs between the two prostrations, and in the state of tashahhud, and to leave placing the right on the left in the state of standing, due to leaving the sunna.) (And) it is disliked (yawning because it is from laziness and fullness; if it overcomes him, let him suppress it as much as he can, even by taking his lip with his teeth, and by placing the back of his right hand or his sleeve in standing, and his left in other than it, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Indeed Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning; so if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as he can and not say 'hah hah,' for that is from the devil who laughs at him.' And in a narration: 'Let him place his hand on his mouth, for the devil enters it.') (And) it is disliked (to close his eyes) except for a benefit, due to his statement: 'When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes,' because it loses the sight of the recommended place, and every limb and part has a share of worship, and seeing what loses khushu', and it distracts the mind; perhaps closing may be better than looking. (And) it is disliked (to raise them to the sky) due to his statement: 'What is the matter with people who raise their eyes to the sky; let them desist or their eyesight will be snatched away.' (And stretching) i.e. laziness, (and the small action that contradicts prayer, and its individuals are many, like plucking a hair, and from it is the throwing of a stone) from Abdullah. Some experts said: One should rely on this restriction because the right hand is designated by the Lawgiver for what is honorable, and the left for what is impure, and the devil is impure, so he is repelled with the left, as in al-Jawahir al-Nafisa, except that covering the mouth with the left during standing is an excessive action, so it is avoided. So in other than standing, he covers with the left due to the absence of the mentioned cause. And in al-Durr, as an appendix to the disliked things, yawning even outside prayer is mentioned due to being from the devil, and prophets are protected from it. His saying: 'Indeed Allah loves sneezing' means He rewards for it because of the praise and supplication that follow. His saying: 'And dislikes yawning' means He does not reward for it, and it is possible that the meaning is that He punishes for it considering its cause, as it is optional like fullness. His saying: 'That is from (the devil)' indicates prohibition, so it is disliked to the degree of prohibition. His saying: 'And in a narration: let him place his hand' etc. From the two hadiths together, one has a choice between suppressing it and placing the hand in his mouth, and the scholars distributed it to the two previous situations. His saying: 'For the devil enters it' does not prevent carrying it literally, for the devil runs in the human as blood runs, or the meaning is that he whispers to him. His saying: 'except for a benefit' as when he closes them to avoid seeing what prevents his khushu', or to perfect his khushu', intending to cut off looking at others and turn to the side of the King, the Forgiver, as in Majma' al-Anhur, and this suffices from his later saying 'and seeing what loses khushu'' etc. His saying: 'Let him not close his eyes' is apparent prohibition; but al-Bahr said: The dislike should be considered tanzihi if it is without necessity or benefit. His saying: 'Because it loses the sight of the recommended place' – the scholars differed on the reasoning for the dislike; some used this hadith, but its chain is weak as in al-Bahr; the author of al-Bada'i used this reasoning; al-Zayla'i reasoned that it contradicts khushu' and is a kind of play; and as in al-Halabi, it is the action of the People of the Book, and this may indicate prohibition. His saying: 'and part' etc. is from 'atf al-khas. His saying: 'and distracts the mind' means it scatters the heart, so it is applying the state to the place, or that what occurs to the mind concerning the truth scatters, so it is literal. His saying: 'What is the matter with people' etc. – scholars said this hadith contains a severe threat for the doer, and may indicate prohibition; consensus has been established on its dislike in prayer due to contradicting the required khushu'. As for outside prayer, the majority permitted it because the sky is the qibla of supplication as the Ka'ba is the qibla of prayer, as stated by 'Allama Nuh. His saying: 'and stretching' means extending, i.e. stretching his hands and exposing his chest; the common people mistake by replacing its ya with 'ayn. His saying: 'from laziness'.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, enumerating disliked actions (makruhat) in prayer. It opens by stating that actions not part of prayer are generally disliked, then specifies: fanning oneself with garment or fan (even once or twice) because it negates khushu'. The commentary discusses whether this invalidates prayer, noting that according to al-Dhakhira, using a fan invalidates even once because observers would be certain the person is not in prayer, unlike using a sleeve. Next, turning fingers from qibla in sujud is disliked based on a hadith to direct limbs toward qibla as much as possible. Not placing hands on knees in ruku, on thighs between sujuds and during tashahhud, and not placing right hand over left in qiyam are disliked for leaving sunna. Yawning is disliked because it stems from laziness and fullness; one should suppress it by taking the lip with teeth or placing the back of the right hand on the mouth (or sleeve in standing, left hand otherwise). Hadiths confirm Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning, and the devil enters the mouth during a yawn. The commentary notes that based on the hadith 'that is from the devil,' yawning is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). Closing eyes in prayer is disliked except for benefit (e.g., to avoid distractions). Some scholars use a hadith with weak chain; others reason it contradicts khushu' or resembles People of the Book. Al-Bahr says it is tanzihi (lightly disliked) without necessity. Raising eyes to sky is disliked due to a hadith threatening loss of eyesight; consensus agrees on its dislike in prayer, though outside prayer it is permitted as the sky is qibla for supplication. Stretching (tamatti) and small actions contrary to prayer (e.g., plucking a hair) are also disliked. The commentary emphasizes that the basis for these rulings is maintaining khushu' and following the sunna.

Key Terms
مروحة (mirwaha): A hand fan used to create airflow; here with kasr of meem and fatha of waw.
تثاؤب (tathawub): Yawning; considered a disliked action due to laziness and association with the devil.
تغميض العينين (taghmid al-aynayn): Closing the eyes during prayer; disliked unless for a valid benefit.
عمل قليل (amal qalil): Small action that does not invalidate prayer but is disliked if it contradicts khushu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on yawning in prayer?
A) It is haram and invalidates the prayer.
B) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and one should suppress it.
C) It is mubah (permissible) as long as it is not accompanied by sound.
D) It is mustahabb because it relieves the body.

Key Takeaway
Actions that disturb khushu‘ are disliked in prayer, with the degree of dislike determined by the strength of evidence and the severity of the contradiction.

Yawning and Sneezing in Prayer
Commentary on disliked acts in prayer focusing on yawning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on yawning in prayer and identify the hadith evidence that establishes it as makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Yawning in prayer is from Satan; its prohibition indicates makruh tahrimi.

This lesson examines the ruling on yawning during salah. While sneezing is beloved, yawning is disliked because it is attributed to Satan in authentic hadith. The commentary clarifies the strength of the prohibition and reconciles the two narrations regarding hand placement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sneezing is beloved (muhibb) and yawning is disliked (makruh) in prayer.
The base text uses 'يكره' indicating dislike.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning...' is the primary evidence.
The hadith includes a command to suppress yawning.
3
Analyze the Hanafi position
The prohibition (nahy) in the hadith indicates makruh tahrimi in Hanafi usul, not just tanzih.
Different opinions on the cause of dislike do not affect the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
العطاس ويكره التثاؤب فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده ما استطاع ولا يقول هاه هاه فإنما ذلكم من الشيطان يضحك منه وفي رواية فليمسك يده على فمه فإنّ الشيطان يدخل فيه (و) يكره (تغميض عينيه) إلا لمصلحة لقوله الله : إذا قام أحدكم في الصلاة فلا يغمض عينيه لأنه يفوت النظر للمحل المندوب ولكل عضو وطرف حظ من العبادة وبرؤية ما يفوت الخشوع ويفرق الخاطر ربما يكون التغميض أولى من النظر (و) يكره (رفعهما للسماء) لقوله : ما بال أقوام يرفعون أبصارهم إلى السماء لينتهن أو لتخطفن أبصارهم (والتمطي) التكاسل ( والعمل القليل المنافي للصلاة، وأفراده كثيرة كنتف شعرة، ومنه الرمية عن القوس مرة في صلاة الخوف كالمشي في صلاته (و) منه (أخذ قملة وقتلها من غير عذر فإن تشغله بالعض كنملة، وبرغوت لا يكره الأخذ ويحترز عن دمها لقول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى بنجاسة قشرها ودمها ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد وتغطية أنفه وفمه) لما روينا (و) يكره (وضع شيء) لا يذوب (في فمه) وهو (يمنع القراءة المسنونة) أو يشغل باله كذهب (و) يكره السجود على كور (عمامته من غير ضرورة حر أو برد أو خشونة أرض والكور دور من أدوارها بفتح الكاف إذا كان على الجبهة لأنه حائل لا يمنع السجود أما إذا كان على الرأس وسجد عليه ولم تصب جبهته الأرض لا تصح صلاته وكثير من العوام يفعله (و) يكره السجود على صورة ذي روح لأنه يشبه عبادتها (و) يكره
فقد قال في الحديث: إن الله يحب العطاس ويكره التثاؤب، فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده ما استطاع ولا يقول هاه هاه فإنما ذلكم من الشيطان يضحك منه، وفي رواية فليمسك يده على فمه فإن الشيطان يدخل فيه، واختلف تعليل الكراهة فقيل للحديث، وقيل لأنه يفوت الخشوع، وقيل لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب، وربما يفيد التحريم. وقوله: (والتمطي) أي التمدد، وهو مد يديه وإبداء صدره والعامة يخطئون بإبدال يائه عيناً. وقوله: (من التكاسل) فظاهره أنه مكروه تنزيهاً. وقوله: (المنافي للصلاة) أما المطلوب فيها فهو منها كتحريك الأصابع لعد التسبيح في صلاته. وقوله: (كنتف شعرة أو شعرتين) كذا في الشرح. وقوله: (كالمشي في صلاته) أي صلاة الخوف ظاهره أنه مكروه، وهو مطلوب ويحتمل أن الضمير يرجع إلى المصلي لا بقيد صلاة الخوف ولا شك في كراهته. وقوله: (ومنه أخذ قلة) أي التعرض لها عند عدم الإيذاء، وقوله: (لا يكره الأخذ) لأن تركها يذهب الخشوع ويشغل القلب بالألم. وقوله: (ويحترز الخ) أي عن دمها لقول الإمام الشافعي بنجاسة قشرها ودمها ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد للنهي عن تقديره ولو بطاهر. وقوله: (لما روينا) من أنه نهى عن أن يغطي الرجل فاه. وقوله: (لا يذوب) احترز به عما يذوب كالسكر يكون في فيه إذا ابتلع ذوبه فإنها تفسد. وقوله: (المسنونة) أما إذا منع أصل القراءة أو لزم منه تغيير بما يفسد فسدت. وقوله: (ويكره السجود على كور عمامته) الظاهر أن الكراهة تنزيهية لما نقل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من السجود على كور العمامة تعليماً للجواز، فلم تكن تحريمية. وقوله: (ويكره السجود على صورة ذي روح) الأولى ذكر هذا عند ذكر الصورة فيما يأتي، أو يقدم ما يأتي هنا لجمع الكلام المتناسب، وفي النهر أشدها كراهة أن تكون أمام المصلى ثم فوق رأسه بحذائه ثم خلفه.
Book of Prayer. Sneezing is beloved and yawning is disliked. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. (And) it is disliked (to close his eyes) except for a benefit, because the Prophet said: When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes; for it misses the recommended direction of sight, and every limb and part has a share in worship, and seeing what breaks concentration and distracts the mind. Sometimes closing the eyes may be preferable to looking. (And) it is disliked (to raise them to the sky) because he said: What is wrong with people who raise their eyes to the sky? Let them desist or their eyes will be snatched away. (And stretching) i.e., laziness. (And a small action that contradicts prayer, and its instances are many, such as plucking a hair; and from it is shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear, like walking during his prayer.) (And) from it (is taking a louse and killing it without an excuse; but if it disturbs him by biting like an ant or a mosquito, taking it is not disliked, and he avoids its blood because of the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i – may Allah have mercy on him – about the impurity of its shell and blood. And it is not permissible in our view to throw its shell in the mosque. And covering his nose and mouth) because of what we narrated. (And) it is disliked (to put something) that does not melt (in his mouth) which (prevents the recommended recitation) or distracts his mind like gold. (And) it is disliked to prostrate on the fold (of his turban without necessity of heat, cold, or rough ground, and 'fold' is a coil from its coils with fatihah on the kasra if it is on the forehead because it is an obstacle that does not prevent prostration. But if it is on the head and he prostrates on it and his forehead does not touch the ground, his prayer is not valid; and many common people do this.) (And) it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being because it resembles worshipping it. (And) it is disliked... The hadith says: Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. The cause of dislike is differed: some say due to the hadith, some say because it misses khushu', some say because it is the practice of the People of the Book; and perhaps it indicates prohibition. His saying: (and stretching) i.e., extending, which is extending his hands and protruding his chest; common people err by replacing its ya with ayn. His saying: (due to laziness) so apparently it is disliked tanzihan. His saying: (contradicts prayer) as for what is sought in it, it is part of it, like moving fingers for counting tasbih in his prayer. His saying: (like plucking a hair or two) thus in the commentary. His saying: (like walking in his prayer) i.e., the fear prayer; apparently it is disliked, but it is sought; and it is possible the pronoun refers to the one praying without the restriction of fear prayer, and there is no doubt it is disliked. His saying: (and from it is taking a louse) i.e., exposing oneself to it when there is no harm; his saying: (taking it is not disliked) because leaving it removes khushu' and preoccupies the heart with pain. His saying: (and he avoids) i.e., its blood because of Imam al-Shafi'i's statement about the impurity of its shell and blood, and it is not permissible in our view to throw its shell in the mosque due to the prohibition of defiling it even with something pure. His saying: (because of what we narrated) that he forbade covering the mouth. His saying: (does not melt) excludes what melts, like sugar in the mouth; if he swallows its melt, it invalidates. His saying: (recommended) as for if it prevents the original recitation or necessitates a change that invalidates, then it invalidates. His saying: (and it is disliked to prostrate on the fold of his turban) apparently the dislike is tanzihi because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated on the fold of his turban as a teaching of permissibility, so it was not tahrimi. His saying: (and it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being) it is better to mention this when mentioning images later, or to bring forward what follows to gather related speech; and in al-Nahr, the most severe dislike is if it is in front of the worshipper, then above his head opposite him, then behind him.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses various disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, providing evidences and refining the rulings. The commentary follows the order of the base text. It begins with yawning: while sneezing is beloved (due to resulting praise and supplication), yawning is disliked, with strong evidence from hadith that it is from Satan. The commentator notes that the hadith's prohibition (nahy) indicates makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). For the hand placement, the commentator synthesizes two hadiths: one suggests suppressing the yawn, another suggests covering the mouth. Scholars reconciled this by applying each to different situations (e.g., if one can suppress, do so; otherwise cover). For closing the eyes, the dislike is tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) unless there is a benefit such as enhancing khushu'. The commentator quotes conflicting opinions and concludes that if it aids concentration, it may be preferable. Raising the eyes to the sky is disliked due to a severe threat in hadith, and consensus holds it is disliked in prayer; outside prayer it is permitted as the sky is the qibla of supplication. Stretching (al-tamatti) is laziness and disliked as it contradicts the spirit of prayer. Small actions that contradict prayer, such as plucking hair or shooting an arrow in the fear prayer, are disliked; however, necessary actions like walking in the fear prayer are permissible. Killing a louse without being bothered is disliked, but if it bites and disturbs concentration, it is not disliked because leaving it would harm khushu'. The commentary includes a reference to Imam al-Shafi'i's view on impurity of lice blood, noting that Hanafis do not consider it najis but still avoid throwing shells in the mosque. Covering the nose and mouth is disliked based on a hadith forbidding it. Putting something in the mouth that does not melt (like a gold piece) is disliked if it prevents recommended recitation or distracts. Prostrating on a fold of the turban is disliked tanzihan, as the Prophet did it to teach permissibility; but if the forehead does not touch the ground due to the turban, the prayer is invalid. Prostrating on an image of a living being is disliked due to resemblance to idol worship, and the dislike is more severe if the image is in front of the worshipper.

Key Terms
التثاؤب (al-tathā'ub): Yawning; considered a disliked act in prayer because it is from Satan according to hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on yawning in prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Haram
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Makruh tanzih
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Yawning in prayer is from Satan and must be suppressed; it is makruh tahrimi.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
5 min
Closing Eyes and Raising Eyes to Sky in Prayer
Commentary on disliked actions of the eyes in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on closing eyes and raising eyes to the sky during prayer, and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Closing eyes is disliked unless for khushu'; raising eyes to sky is severely warned against.

This lesson covers two actions related to the eyes during prayer: closing them and raising them to the sky. Both are disliked but with different degrees. The hadith about raising eyes contains a severe threat, while closing eyes is discouraged because it misses the recommended focus and may reduce khushu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two actions and their rulings
Both are disliked: closing eyes (makruh tanzih) and raising eyes to sky (makruh tahrimi based on the threat).
The base text uses 'يكره' for both.
2
Examine the evidence for each
For closing eyes: a hadith forbids it generally, but an exception is made for benefit. For raising eyes: a hadith threatens to snatch away sight.
3
Analyze the degree of dislike
The threat of losing sight indicates the prohibition is stronger for raising eyes, likely makruh tahrimi.
Closing eyes is tanzih unless it aids khushu', in which case it may be preferable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
العطاس ويكره التثاؤب فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده ما استطاع ولا يقول هاه هاه فإنما ذلكم من الشيطان يضحك منه وفي رواية فليمسك يده على فمه فإنّ الشيطان يدخل فيه (و) يكره (تغميض عينيه) إلا لمصلحة لقوله الله : إذا قام أحدكم في الصلاة فلا يغمض عينيه لأنه يفوت النظر للمحل المندوب ولكل عضو وطرف حظ من العبادة وبرؤية ما يفوت الخشوع ويفرق الخاطر ربما يكون التغميض أولى من النظر (و) يكره (رفعهما للسماء) لقوله : ما بال أقوام يرفعون أبصارهم إلى السماء لينتهن أو لتخطفن أبصارهم (والتمطي) التكاسل ( والعمل القليل المنافي للصلاة، وأفراده كثيرة كنتف شعرة، ومنه الرمية عن القوس مرة في صلاة الخوف كالمشي في صلاته (و) منه (أخذ قملة وقتلها من غير عذر فإن تشغله بالعض كنملة، وبرغوت لا يكره الأخذ ويحترز عن دمها لقول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى بنجاسة قشرها ودمها ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد وتغطية أنفه وفمه) لما روينا (و) يكره (وضع شيء) لا يذوب (في فمه) وهو (يمنع القراءة المسنونة) أو يشغل باله كذهب (و) يكره السجود على كور (عمامته من غير ضرورة حر أو برد أو خشونة أرض والكور دور من أدوارها بفتح الكاف إذا كان على الجبهة لأنه حائل لا يمنع السجود أما إذا كان على الرأس وسجد عليه ولم تصب جبهته الأرض لا تصح صلاته وكثير من العوام يفعله (و) يكره السجود على صورة ذي روح لأنه يشبه عبادتها (و) يكره

Book of Prayer. Sneezing is beloved and yawning is disliked. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. Let them desist or their eyes will be snatched away. (And stretching) i.e., laziness. (And a small action that contradicts prayer, and its instances are many, such as plucking a hair; and from it is shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear, like walking during his prayer.)
