Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses various disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, providing evidences and refining the rulings. The commentary follows the order of the base text. It begins with yawning: while sneezing is beloved (due to resulting praise and supplication), yawning is disliked, with strong evidence from hadith that it is from Satan. The commentator notes that the hadith's prohibition (nahy) indicates makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). For the hand placement, the commentator synthesizes two hadiths: one suggests suppressing the yawn, another suggests covering the mouth. Scholars reconciled this by applying each to different situations (e.g., if one can suppress, do so; otherwise cover). For closing the eyes, the dislike is tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) unless there is a benefit such as enhancing khushu'. The commentator quotes conflicting opinions and concludes that if it aids concentration, it may be preferable. Raising the eyes to the sky is disliked due to a severe threat in hadith, and consensus holds it is disliked in prayer; outside prayer it is permitted as the sky is the qibla of supplication. Stretching (al-tamatti) is laziness and disliked as it contradicts the spirit of prayer. Small actions that contradict prayer, such as plucking hair or shooting an arrow in the fear prayer, are disliked; however, necessary actions like walking in the fear prayer are permissible. Killing a louse without being bothered is disliked, but if it bites and disturbs concentration, it is not disliked because leaving it would harm khushu'. The commentary includes a reference to Imam al-Shafi'i's view on impurity of lice blood, noting that Hanafis do not consider it najis but still avoid throwing shells in the mosque. Covering the nose and mouth is disliked based on a hadith forbidding it. Putting something in the mouth that does not melt (like a gold piece) is disliked if it prevents recommended recitation or distracts. Prostrating on a fold of the turban is disliked tanzihan, as the Prophet did it to teach permissibility; but if the forehead does not touch the ground due to the turban, the prayer is invalid. Prostrating on an image of a living being is disliked due to resemblance to idol worship, and the dislike is more severe if the image is in front of the worshipper.

Key Terms
تغميض العينين (taghmīḍ al-'aynayn): Closing the eyes during prayer; disliked unless for a benefit like increasing khushu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on raising eyes to the sky during prayer?
A) Makruh tanzih
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Closing eyes is makruh tanzih with exception; raising eyes to sky is makruh tahrimi.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Stretching and Small Actions in Prayer
Commentary on stretching and small actions in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify stretching and small actions that contradict prayer as disliked, and distinguish between makruh tanzih and permissible actions.

Core Idea
Stretching due to laziness is disliked; small actions are disliked unless they are part of the prayer's benefit.

This lesson covers stretching (al-tamatti) and various small actions that are considered contradictory to the spirit of prayer. The commentary clarifies that actions like plucking a hair or shooting an arrow in the fear prayer are disliked, but essential actions like walking in the fear prayer are permissible. The key is whether the action is part of the prayer's required movements or not.

Guided Path
1
Define al-tamatti and its ruling
Stretching the body, especially extending hands and chest, is disliked (makruh tanzih) because it indicates laziness.
The base text adds 'التكاسل' (laziness).
2
Identify small actions that contradict prayer
Examples: plucking a hair, shooting an arrow once in the fear prayer, walking during prayer.
These are disliked if they are extra and unnecessary.
3
Distinguish between disliked and permissible
Actions that are part of the prayer (like moving fingers for counting tasbih) are not disliked; necessary actions in fear prayer are permissible despite appearance.
The commentary emphasizes that the fear prayer requires some movement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
العطاس ويكره التثاؤب فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده ما استطاع ولا يقول هاه هاه فإنما ذلكم من الشيطان يضحك منه وفي رواية فليمسك يده على فمه فإنّ الشيطان يدخل فيه (و) يكره (تغميض عينيه) إلا لمصلحة لقوله الله : إذا قام أحدكم في الصلاة فلا يغمض عينيه لأنه يفوت النظر للمحل المندوب ولكل عضو وطرف حظ من العبادة وبرؤية ما يفوت الخشوع ويفرق الخاطر ربما يكون التغميض أولى من النظر (و) يكره (رفعهما للسماء) لقوله : ما بال أقوام يرفعون أبصارهم إلى السماء لينتهن أو لتخطفن أبصارهم (والتمطي) التكاسل ( والعمل القليل المنافي للصلاة، وأفراده كثيرة كنتف شعرة، ومنه الرمية عن القوس مرة في صلاة الخوف كالمشي في صلاته (و) منه (أخذ قملة وقتلها من غير عذر فإن تشغله بالعض كنملة، وبرغوت لا يكره الأخذ ويحترز عن دمها لقول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى بنجاسة قشرها ودمها ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد وتغطية أنفه وفمه) لما روينا (و) يكره (وضع شيء) لا يذوب (في فمه) وهو (يمنع القراءة المسنونة) أو يشغل باله كذهب (و) يكره السجود على كور (عمامته من غير ضرورة حر أو برد أو خشونة أرض والكور دور من أدوارها بفتح الكاف إذا كان على الجبهة لأنه حائل لا يمنع السجود أما إذا كان على الرأس وسجد عليه ولم تصب جبهته الأرض لا تصح صلاته وكثير من العوام يفعله (و) يكره السجود على صورة ذي روح لأنه يشبه عبادتها (و) يكره
فقد قال في الحديث: إن الله يحب العطاس ويكره التثاؤب، فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده ما استطاع ولا يقول هاه هاه فإنما ذلكم من الشيطان يضحك منه، وفي رواية فليمسك يده على فمه فإن الشيطان يدخل فيه، واختلف تعليل الكراهة فقيل للحديث، وقيل لأنه يفوت الخشوع، وقيل لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب، وربما يفيد التحريم. وقوله: (والتمطي) أي التمدد، وهو مد يديه وإبداء صدره والعامة يخطئون بإبدال يائه عيناً. وقوله: (من التكاسل) فظاهره أنه مكروه تنزيهاً. وقوله: (المنافي للصلاة) أما المطلوب فيها فهو منها كتحريك الأصابع لعد التسبيح في صلاته. وقوله: (كنتف شعرة أو شعرتين) كذا في الشرح. وقوله: (كالمشي في صلاته) أي صلاة الخوف ظاهره أنه مكروه، وهو مطلوب ويحتمل أن الضمير يرجع إلى المصلي لا بقيد صلاة الخوف ولا شك في كراهته. وقوله: (ومنه أخذ قلة) أي التعرض لها عند عدم الإيذاء، وقوله: (لا يكره الأخذ) لأن تركها يذهب الخشوع ويشغل القلب بالألم. وقوله: (ويحترز الخ) أي عن دمها لقول الإمام الشافعي بنجاسة قشرها ودمها ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد للنهي عن تقديره ولو بطاهر. وقوله: (لما روينا) من أنه نهى عن أن يغطي الرجل فاه. وقوله: (لا يذوب) احترز به عما يذوب كالسكر يكون في فيه إذا ابتلع ذوبه فإنها تفسد. وقوله: (المسنونة) أما إذا منع أصل القراءة أو لزم منه تغيير بما يفسد فسدت. وقوله: (ويكره السجود على كور عمامته) الظاهر أن الكراهة تنزيهية لما نقل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من السجود على كور العمامة تعليماً للجواز، فلم تكن تحريمية. وقوله: (ويكره السجود على صورة ذي روح) الأولى ذكر هذا عند ذكر الصورة فيما يأتي، أو يقدم ما يأتي هنا لجمع الكلام المتناسب، وفي النهر أشدها كراهة أن تكون أمام المصلى ثم فوق رأسه بحذائه ثم خلفه.
Book of Prayer. Sneezing is beloved and yawning is disliked. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. (And) it is disliked (to close his eyes) except for a benefit, because the Prophet said: When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes; for it misses the recommended direction of sight, and every limb and part has a share in worship, and seeing what breaks concentration and distracts the mind. Sometimes closing the eyes may be preferable to looking. (And) it is disliked (to raise them to the sky) because he said: What is wrong with people who raise their eyes to the sky? Let them desist or their eyes will be snatched away. (And stretching) i.e., laziness. (And a small action that contradicts prayer, and its instances are many, such as plucking a hair; and from it is shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear, like walking during his prayer.) (And) from it (is taking a louse and killing it without an excuse; but if it disturbs him by biting like an ant or a mosquito, taking it is not disliked, and he avoids its blood because of the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i – may Allah have mercy on him – about the impurity of its shell and blood. And it is not permissible in our view to throw its shell in the mosque. And covering his nose and mouth) because of what we narrated. (And) it is disliked (to put something) that does not melt (in his mouth) which (prevents the recommended recitation) or distracts his mind like gold. (And) it is disliked to prostrate on the fold (of his turban without necessity of heat, cold, or rough ground, and 'fold' is a coil from its coils with fatihah on the kasra if it is on the forehead because it is an obstacle that does not prevent prostration. But if it is on the head and he prostrates on it and his forehead does not touch the ground, his prayer is not valid; and many common people do this.) (And) it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being because it resembles worshipping it. (And) it is disliked... The hadith says: Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. The cause of dislike is differed: some say due to the hadith, some say because it misses khushu', some say because it is the practice of the People of the Book; and perhaps it indicates prohibition. His saying: (and stretching) i.e., extending, which is extending his hands and protruding his chest; common people err by replacing its ya with ayn. His saying: (due to laziness) so apparently it is disliked tanzihan. His saying: (contradicts prayer) as for what is sought in it, it is part of it, like moving fingers for counting tasbih in his prayer. His saying: (like plucking a hair or two) thus in the commentary. His saying: (like walking in his prayer) i.e., the fear prayer; apparently it is disliked, but it is sought; and it is possible the pronoun refers to the one praying without the restriction of fear prayer, and there is no doubt it is disliked. His saying: (and from it is taking a louse) i.e., exposing oneself to it when there is no harm; his saying: (taking it is not disliked) because leaving it removes khushu' and preoccupies the heart with pain. His saying: (and he avoids) i.e., its blood because of Imam al-Shafi'i's statement about the impurity of its shell and blood, and it is not permissible in our view to throw its shell in the mosque due to the prohibition of defiling it even with something pure. His saying: (because of what we narrated) that he forbade covering the mouth. His saying: (does not melt) excludes what melts, like sugar in the mouth; if he swallows its melt, it invalidates. His saying: (recommended) as for if it prevents the original recitation or necessitates a change that invalidates, then it invalidates. His saying: (and it is disliked to prostrate on the fold of his turban) apparently the dislike is tanzihi because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated on the fold of his turban as a teaching of permissibility, so it was not tahrimi. His saying: (and it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being) it is better to mention this when mentioning images later, or to bring forward what follows to gather related speech; and in al-Nahr, the most severe dislike is if it is in front of the worshipper, then above his head opposite him, then behind him.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses various disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, providing evidences and refining the rulings. The commentary follows the order of the base text. It begins with yawning: while sneezing is beloved (due to resulting praise and supplication), yawning is disliked, with strong evidence from hadith that it is from Satan. The commentator notes that the hadith's prohibition (nahy) indicates makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). For the hand placement, the commentator synthesizes two hadiths: one suggests suppressing the yawn, another suggests covering the mouth. Scholars reconciled this by applying each to different situations (e.g., if one can suppress, do so; otherwise cover). For closing the eyes, the dislike is tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) unless there is a benefit such as enhancing khushu'. The commentator quotes conflicting opinions and concludes that if it aids concentration, it may be preferable. Raising the eyes to the sky is disliked due to a severe threat in hadith, and consensus holds it is disliked in prayer; outside prayer it is permitted as the sky is the qibla of supplication. Stretching (al-tamatti) is laziness and disliked as it contradicts the spirit of prayer. Small actions that contradict prayer, such as plucking hair or shooting an arrow in the fear prayer, are disliked; however, necessary actions like walking in the fear prayer are permissible. Killing a louse without being bothered is disliked, but if it bites and disturbs concentration, it is not disliked because leaving it would harm khushu'. The commentary includes a reference to Imam al-Shafi'i's view on impurity of lice blood, noting that Hanafis do not consider it najis but still avoid throwing shells in the mosque. Covering the nose and mouth is disliked based on a hadith forbidding it. Putting something in the mouth that does not melt (like a gold piece) is disliked if it prevents recommended recitation or distracts. Prostrating on a fold of the turban is disliked tanzihan, as the Prophet did it to teach permissibility; but if the forehead does not touch the ground due to the turban, the prayer is invalid. Prostrating on an image of a living being is disliked due to resemblance to idol worship, and the dislike is more severe if the image is in front of the worshipper.

Key Terms
التمطي (al-tamattu'): Stretching the body, especially extending hands and chest; a disliked action indicating laziness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on plucking a hair during prayer?
A) It invalidates the prayer
B) It is makruh tanzih
C) It is permissible
D) It is mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Stretching and unnecessary small actions are makruh tanzih; necessary actions like walking in fear prayer are permissible.

Lice and Covering Mouth/Nose in Prayer
Commentary on lice and covering face in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on killing a louse and covering the nose/mouth during prayer, and identify the related evidence.

Core Idea
Killing a louse without excuse is disliked; if it bites, it is allowed. Covering nose/mouth is disliked based on hadith.

This lesson addresses actions related to insects and covering the face during prayer. Killing a louse without being bothered is disliked because it distracts; but if it bites, it may be removed to maintain concentration. Covering the nose and mouth is disliked according to a prophetic prohibition. The commentary also includes a note on Imam al-Shafi'i's view about impurity of lice blood, which Hanafis do not follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings on lice
Killing a louse without excuse is disliked; if it bites, it is not disliked to remove it.
Avoiding its blood is recommended due to difference of opinion.
2
Identify the ruling on covering nose/mouth
It is disliked based on the hadith forbidding it.
The commentator references 'lama rawayna' (what we narrated).
3
Understand the cross-madhhab reference
Imam al-Shafi'i considers lice blood impure; Hanafis do not, but still avoid throwing shells in the mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
العطاس ويكره التثاؤب فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليرده ما استطاع ولا يقول هاه هاه فإنما ذلكم من الشيطان يضحك منه وفي رواية فليمسك يده على فمه فإنّ الشيطان يدخل فيه (و) يكره (تغميض عينيه) إلا لمصلحة لقوله الله : إذا قام أحدكم في الصلاة فلا يغمض عينيه لأنه يفوت النظر للمحل المندوب ولكل عضو وطرف حظ من العبادة وبرؤية ما يفوت الخشوع ويفرق الخاطر ربما يكون التغميض أولى من النظر (و) يكره (رفعهما للسماء) لقوله : ما بال أقوام يرفعون أبصارهم إلى السماء لينتهن أو لتخطفن أبصارهم (والتمطي) التكاسل ( والعمل القليل المنافي للصلاة، وأفراده كثيرة كنتف شعرة، ومنه الرمية عن القوس مرة في صلاة الخوف كالمشي في صلاته (و) منه (أخذ قملة وقتلها من غير عذر فإن تشغله بالعض كنملة، وبرغوت لا يكره الأخذ ويحترز عن دمها لقول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى بنجاسة قشرها ودمها ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد وتغطية أنفه وفمه) لما روينا (و) يكره (وضع شيء) لا يذوب (في فمه) وهو (يمنع القراءة المسنونة) أو يشغل باله كذهب (و) يكره السجود على كور (عمامته من غير ضرورة حر أو برد أو خشونة أرض والكور دور من أدوارها بفتح الكاف إذا كان على الجبهة لأنه حائل لا يمنع السجود أما إذا كان على الرأس وسجد عليه ولم تصب جبهته الأرض لا تصح صلاته وكثير من العوام يفعله (و) يكره السجود على صورة ذي روح لأنه يشبه عبادتها (و) يكره

Book of Prayer. Sneezing is beloved and yawning is disliked. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. Sometimes closing the eyes may be preferable to looking. (And) it is disliked (to raise them to the sky) because he said: What is wrong with people who raise their eyes to the sky? Let them desist or their eyes will be snatched away. (And stretching) i.e., laziness. (And a small action that contradicts prayer, and its instances are many, such as plucking a hair; and from it is shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear, like walking during his prayer.) (And) from it (is taking a louse and killing it without an excuse; but if it disturbs him by biting like an ant or a mosquito, taking it is not disliked, and he avoids its blood because of the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i – may Allah have mercy on him – about the impurity of its shell and blood. (And) it is disliked (to put something) that does not melt (in his mouth) which (prevents the recommended recitation) or distracts his mind like gold. His saying: (due to laziness) so apparently it is disliked tanzihan. His saying: (contradicts prayer) as for what is sought in it, it is part of it, like moving fingers for counting tasbih in his prayer. His saying: (recommended) as for if it prevents the original recitation or necessitates a change that invalidates, then it invalidates. Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses various disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, providing evidences and refining the rulings. The commentary follows the order of the base text. Scholars reconciled this by applying each to different situations (e.g., if one can suppress, do so; otherwise cover). The commentator quotes conflicting opinions and concludes that if it aids concentration, it may be preferable. Raising the eyes to the sky is disliked due to a severe threat in hadith, and consensus holds it is disliked in prayer; outside prayer it is permitted as the sky is the qibla of supplication. Stretching (al-tamatti) is laziness and disliked as it contradicts the spirit of prayer. Small actions that contradict prayer, such as plucking hair or shooting an arrow in the fear prayer, are disliked; however, necessary actions like walking in the fear prayer are permissible. Killing a louse without being bothered is disliked, but if it bites and disturbs concentration, it is not disliked because leaving it would harm khushu'. The commentary includes a reference to Imam al-Shafi'i's view on impurity of lice blood, noting that Hanafis do not consider it najis but still avoid throwing shells in the mosque. Covering the nose and mouth is disliked based on a hadith forbidding it. Putting something in the mouth that does not melt (like a gold piece) is disliked if it prevents recommended recitation or distracts. Prostrating on a fold of the turban is disliked tanzihan, as the Prophet did it to teach permissibility; but if the forehead does not touch the ground due to the turban, the prayer is invalid. Prostrating on an image of a living being is disliked due to resemblance to idol worship, and the dislike is more severe if the image is in front of the worshipper.

Key Terms
التثاؤب (al-tathā'ub): Yawning (not directly in this lesson, but key term from overall passage)

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is haram
D) It is mustahabb

Putting Objects in Mouth and Prostration on Turban/Image
Commentary on objects in mouth and prostration details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on putting non-melting objects in the mouth and prostrating on turban folds or on images of living beings during prayer.

Core Idea
Putting something in the mouth that prevents recitation or distracts is disliked; prostration on turban fold is tanzih if forehead touches ground, invalid if not; prostration on images is disliked.

This lesson covers two distinct issues: placing objects in the mouth that do not melt (like a gold piece) and prostration on turban folds or on images. The commentary clarifies that if the object prevents recommended recitation or distracts, it is disliked. Prostration on a turban fold is disliked (tanzih) if the forehead still touches the ground; but if the forehead does not touch, the prayer is invalid. Prostration on images of living beings is disliked due to resemblance to idol worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on placing something in the mouth
It is disliked if it prevents the recommended recitation or distracts the mind.
If it melts (like sugar) and is swallowed, it invalidates.
2
Identify the ruling on prostration on turban fold
Disliked (tanzih) if the forehead touches the ground; invalid if the forehead is blocked.
The Prophet did it to teach permissibility.
3
Identify the ruling on prostration on an image
Disliked due to resemblance to idol worship; severity increases if image is in front.
This is a separate disliked act.

Book of Prayer. Sneezing is beloved and yawning is disliked. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. (And) it is disliked (to close his eyes) except for a benefit, because the Prophet said: When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes; for it misses the recommended direction of sight, and every limb and part has a share in worship, and seeing what breaks concentration and distracts the mind. Sometimes closing the eyes may be preferable to looking. (And) it is disliked (to raise them to the sky) because he said: What is wrong with people who raise their eyes to the sky? Let them desist or their eyes will be snatched away. (And stretching) i.e., laziness. (And a small action that contradicts prayer, and its instances are many, such as plucking a hair; and from it is shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear, like walking during his prayer.) (And) from it (is taking a louse and killing it without an excuse; but if it disturbs him by biting like an ant or a mosquito, taking it is not disliked, and he avoids its blood because of the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i – may Allah have mercy on him – about the impurity of its shell and blood. But if it is on the head and he prostrates on it and his forehead does not touch the ground, his prayer is not valid; and many common people do this.) (And) it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being because it resembles worshipping it. (And) it is disliked... The hadith says: Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning. So if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible and not say 'hah hah'; for that is from Satan, who laughs at him. In another narration: let him place his hand over his mouth, for Satan enters through it. The cause of dislike is differed: some say due to the hadith, some say because it misses khushu', some say because it is the practice of the People of the Book; and perhaps it indicates prohibition. His saying: (and stretching) i.e., extending, which is extending his hands and protruding his chest; common people err by replacing its ya with ayn. His saying: (due to laziness) so apparently it is disliked tanzihan. His saying: (contradicts prayer) as for what is sought in it, it is part of it, like moving fingers for counting tasbih in his prayer. His saying: (like plucking a hair or two) thus in the commentary. His saying: (like walking in his prayer) i.e., the fear prayer; apparently it is disliked, but it is sought; and it is possible the pronoun refers to the one praying without the restriction of fear prayer, and there is no doubt it is disliked. His saying: (and from it is taking a louse) i.e., exposing oneself to it when there is no harm; his saying: (taking it is not disliked) because leaving it removes khushu' and preoccupies the heart with pain. His saying: (and he avoids) i.e., its blood because of Imam al-Shafi'i's statement about the impurity of its shell and blood, and it is not permissible in our view to throw its shell in the mosque due to the prohibition of defiling it even with something pure. His saying: (because of what we narrated) that he forbade covering the mouth. His saying: (does not melt) excludes what melts, like sugar in the mouth; if he swallows its melt, it invalidates. His saying: (recommended) as for if it prevents the original recitation or necessitates a change that invalidates, then it invalidates. His saying: (and it is disliked to prostrate on the fold of his turban) apparently the dislike is tanzihi because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated on the fold of his turban as a teaching of permissibility, so it was not tahrimi. His saying: (and it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being) it is better to mention this when mentioning images later, or to bring forward what follows to gather related speech; and in al-Nahr, the most severe dislike is if it is in front of the worshipper, then above his head opposite him, then behind him.

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses various disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, providing evidences and refining the rulings. The commentary follows the order of the base text. It begins with yawning: while sneezing is beloved (due to resulting praise and supplication), yawning is disliked, with strong evidence from hadith that it is from Satan. The commentator notes that the hadith's prohibition (nahy) indicates makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). For the hand placement, the commentator synthesizes two hadiths: one suggests suppressing the yawn, another suggests covering the mouth. Scholars reconciled this by applying each to different situations (e.g., if one can suppress, do so; otherwise cover). For closing the eyes, the dislike is tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) unless there is a benefit such as enhancing khushu'. The commentator quotes conflicting opinions and concludes that if it aids concentration, it may be preferable. Raising the eyes to the sky is disliked due to a severe threat in hadith, and consensus holds it is disliked in prayer; outside prayer it is permitted as the sky is the qibla of supplication. Stretching (al-tamatti) is laziness and disliked as it contradicts the spirit of prayer. Small actions that contradict prayer, such as plucking hair or shooting an arrow in the fear prayer, are disliked; however, necessary actions like walking in the fear prayer are permissible. Killing a louse without being bothered is disliked, but if it bites and disturbs concentration, it is not disliked because leaving it would harm khushu'. The commentary includes a reference to Imam al-Shafi'i's view on impurity of lice blood, noting that Hanafis do not consider it najis but still avoid throwing shells in the mosque. Covering the nose and mouth is disliked based on a hadith forbidding it. Putting something in the mouth that does not melt (like a gold piece) is disliked if it prevents recommended recitation or distracts. Prostrating on a fold of the turban is disliked tanzihan, as the Prophet did it to teach permissibility; but if the forehead does not touch the ground due to the turban, the prayer is invalid. Prostrating on an image of a living being is disliked due to resemblance to idol worship, and the dislike is more severe if the image is in front of the worshipper.

Shooting an Arrow During Fear Prayer
Discusses permissibility of shooting arrow and taking lice during fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shooting an arrow once during fear prayer and explain the qiyas (analogy) that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
Shooting an arrow once in fear prayer is mubah by analogy to walking, despite the general dislike of extraneous movement.

In the fear prayer (salat al-khawf), certain movements are allowed for necessity. This lesson focuses on the specific action of shooting an arrow once. The passage clarifies that while extra movements are generally disliked, shooting an arrow is permissible when needed, just as walking during the prayer is permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its apparent ruling
Locate the matn: 'Shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear is like walking in his prayer.' Notice that the matn compares it to walking, which is already permitted.
The apparent meaning from the matn is that it is mildly disliked (makruh tanzih), as stated in the commentary.
2
Recognize the need (hajah) as the illa
The commentary explains that walking is allowed due to necessity, and by analogy (qiyas), shooting an arrow is also permissible because of the same need (defense). The need overrides the general dislike.
The illa (effective cause) is the need for the action during the prayer of fear.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
The text mentions that the apparent meaning suggests dislike, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is permissibility. This is an example of how later Hanafi scholars resolved the apparent contradiction.
The commentary emphasizes that the permissibility is the correct position for fatwa.
4
Understand the qiyas structure
Asl (original case): walking in fear prayer is permissible. Far' (new case): shooting an arrow once. Illa: need (hajah). Hukm al-asl: mubah. Hukm al-far': mubah.
The qiyas is valid and not overridden by istihsan here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القوس مرة في صلاة الخوف كالمشي في صلاته (و) منه (أخذ قملة وقتلها من غير عذر فإن تشغله بالعض كنملة، وبرغوت لا يكره الأخذ ويحترز عن دمها لقول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى بنجاسة قشرها ودمها ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد وتغطية أنفه وفمه) لما روينا
فظاهره انه مكروه تنزيهاً . قوله : (المنافي للصلاة) أما المطلوب فيها فهو منها كتحريك الأصابع لعد التسبيح في صلاته قوله : (كنتف شعرة أو شعرتين كذا في الشرح. قوله: (كالمشي في صلاته أي صلاة الخوف ظاهره أنه مكروه، وهو مطلوب ويحتمل أن الضمير يرجع إلى المصلي، لا بقيد صلاة الخوف، ولا شك في كراهته، وأفاد في الشرح أن الرمي مرة فيها مباح كالمشي فيها، فقال لأنه لما أبيح له المشي فكذا الرمية لاحتياجه إليها اهـ، والموجب لهذا الخلل قصد الاختصار . قوله : (ومنه أخذ قلة أي التعرض لها عند عدم الإيذاء. قوله : (لا يكره الأخذ لأن تركها يذهب الخشوع ويشغل القلب بالألم، وتحمل الإساءة والكراهة المروية عن الإمام وأبي يوسف على أخذها قصداً من غير عذر كما في الحلبي، وإذا أخذها بعد التعرض بالإيذاء فإما أن يقتلها، أو يدفنها، والدفن أولى كما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله : ويحترز الخ وهذا في غير المسجد، أما فيه فلا بأس بالقتل بعمل قليل، ولا يطرحها فيه بطريق الدفن، أو غيره مطلقاً سواء كان في الصلاة أم لا لحديث إذا وجد أحدكم القملة في ثيابه فليصرها، ولا يطرحها في المسجد، إلا إذا غلب على ظنه أنه يظفر بها بعد الفراغ من فيخرجها، قوله: (ولا يجوز عندنا إلقاء قشرها في المسجد للنهي عن تقديره ولو بطاهر قاله السيد قوله : (لما روينا من أنه نهى عن أن يغطي الرجل فاه كذا في الشرح
Shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear is like walking in his prayer, and from it is taking a louse and killing it without excuse, and if it distracts him by biting like an ant, and a flea, taking it is not disliked and he should be cautious about its blood due to the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i may Allah have mercy on him regarding the impurity of its shell and blood, and it is not permissible for us to throw its shell in the mosque and covering his nose and mouth because of what we have narrated. So its apparent meaning is that it is mildly disliked. His saying: (that which contradicts the prayer) As for what is sought in it, it is from it, like moving the fingers to count the glorifications in his prayer. His saying: (plucking one or two hairs) similarly in the Sharh. His saying: (like walking in his prayer) meaning the prayer of fear, its apparent meaning is that it is disliked, and it is sought, and it is possible that the pronoun refers to the praying person, not restricted to the prayer of fear, and there is no doubt about its dislike. And it is stated in the Sharh that shooting once in it is permissible like walking in it, because since walking is permitted for him, so too is shooting due to his need for it. The cause for this imperfection is the intent of brevity. His saying: (and from it taking a louse) meaning exposing oneself to it when there is no harm. His saying: (taking it is not disliked) because leaving it removes humility and occupies the heart with pain, and the offense and dislike reported from Imam and Abu Yusuf are interpreted as taking it intentionally without excuse as in al-Halabi. And when he takes it after being harmed, then either he kills it or buries it, and burying is better as the author indicated by his saying: 'and he should be cautious' etc. This is outside the mosque; as for inside, there is no harm in killing with a small act, and he should not throw it there by burying or otherwise, whether in prayer or not, due to the hadith: 'If one of you finds a louse in his garment, let him squeeze it and not throw it in the mosque,' unless he thinks it likely that he will retrieve it after finishing, so he may remove it. His saying: (it is not permissible for us to throw its shell in the mosque) due to the prohibition of its estimation, even if by a pure thing, as said by al-Sayyid. His saying: (because of what we have narrated) that he forbade a man from covering his mouth, as in the Sharh.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya commentary. It begins by addressing the ruling of shooting an arrow once during the fear prayer: it is permissible (mubah) like walking, and not disliked as some might think. The commentary clarifies that the apparent meaning is mildly disliked (makruh tanzihan) but the primary position is that it is permissible due to necessity. The second part discusses taking and killing lice. The ruling: taking a louse without excuse is disliked (makruh) according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but if it distracts by biting, it is not disliked—in fact, it is recommended to remove the distraction. The commentary explains that the reported dislike refers to intentional removal without cause. Killing is permissible, but burying is preferred over throwing. Covering the nose and mouth is prohibited based on a hadith. The passage also addresses the impurity of the louse's shell according to Imam al-Shafi'i, but the Hanafi position is that it is pure, yet throwing it in the mosque is disliked due to general prohibition.

Key Terms
قوس (qaws): Bow (used for shooting arrows); here it refers to the action of shooting an arrow once during fear prayer.
صلاة الخوف (salāt al-khawf): Fear prayer – a shortened and modified prayer performed during battle or danger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on shooting an arrow once during fear prayer?
A) Makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
B) Mubah (permissible)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Sunnah (recommended)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits shooting an arrow once in fear prayer based on qiyas to walking, overcoming the general dislike of extraneous movement in prayer.

Taking and Killing Lice During Prayer
Discusses permissibility of shooting arrow and taking lice during fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi rulings on taking a louse during prayer with and without excuse, and explain the cross-madhhab dispute regarding impurity.

Core Idea
Taking a louse in prayer is makruh tanzih without excuse, but if it distracts, removing it is permissible to preserve khushu.

Lice can be a common disturbance during prayer. This lesson examines the Hanafi position: intentional removal without cause is mildly disliked, but when the louse bites and distracts, it becomes permissible—even recommended—to remove it. The passage also addresses the impurity of the louse's shell and blood, a point of disagreement with the Shafi'i school, and the etiquette of disposal in and out of the mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for two scenarios
The matn distinguishes: (1) taking a louse without excuse is disliked (makruh), (2) if it bites and distracts, taking it is not disliked (i.e., permissible).
The dislike is mild (makruh tanzih), not prohibitive.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf held that taking without excuse is disliked. Some reports from Imam Muhammad may differ. The mufta bihi is that taking when in pain is not disliked.
The commentary interprets the reported dislike as referring to intentional removal without cause.
3
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The hadith: 'If one of you finds a louse in his garment, let him squeeze it, and do not throw it in the mosque.' This indicates permissibility of killing (squeezing) and prohibition of throwing in the mosque.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for this ruling.
4
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the louse's shell and blood impure (najis). The Hanafi school considers them pure, but still dislikes throwing the shell in the mosque due to respect.
The practical difference: Hanafis allow touching the louse's shell without breaking wudu; Shafi'is require washing if contacted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Shooting an arrow once in the prayer of fear is like walking in his prayer, and from it is taking a louse and killing it without excuse, and if it distracts him by biting like an ant, and a flea, taking it is not disliked and he should be cautious about its blood due to the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i may Allah have mercy on him regarding the impurity of its shell and blood, and it is not permissible for us to throw its shell in the mosque and covering his nose and mouth because of what we have narrated. So its apparent meaning is that it is mildly disliked. His saying: (that which contradicts the prayer) As for what is sought in it, it is from it, like moving the fingers to count the glorifications in his prayer. His saying: (plucking one or two hairs) similarly in the Sharh. His saying: (like walking in his prayer) meaning the prayer of fear, its apparent meaning is that it is disliked, and it is sought, and it is possible that the pronoun refers to the praying person, not restricted to the prayer of fear, and there is no doubt about its dislike. And it is stated in the Sharh that shooting once in it is permissible like walking in it, because since walking is permitted for him, so too is shooting due to his need for it. The cause for this imperfection is the intent of brevity. His saying: (and from it taking a louse) meaning exposing oneself to it when there is no harm. His saying: (taking it is not disliked) because leaving it removes humility and occupies the heart with pain, and the offense and dislike reported from Imam and Abu Yusuf are interpreted as taking it intentionally without excuse as in al-Halabi. And when he takes it after being harmed, then either he kills it or buries it, and burying is better as the author indicated by his saying: 'and he should be cautious' etc. This is outside the mosque; as for inside, there is no harm in killing with a small act, and he should not throw it there by burying or otherwise, whether in prayer or not, due to the hadith: 'If one of you finds a louse in his garment, let him squeeze it and not throw it in the mosque,' unless he thinks it likely that he will retrieve it after finishing, so he may remove it. His saying: (it is not permissible for us to throw its shell in the mosque) due to the prohibition of its estimation, even if by a pure thing, as said by al-Sayyid. His saying: (because of what we have narrated) that he forbade a man from covering his mouth, as in the Sharh.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya commentary. It begins by addressing the ruling of shooting an arrow once during the fear prayer: it is permissible (mubah) like walking, and not disliked as some might think. The commentary clarifies that the apparent meaning is mildly disliked (makruh tanzihan) but the primary position is that it is permissible due to necessity. The second part discusses taking and killing lice. The ruling: taking a louse without excuse is disliked (makruh) according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but if it distracts by biting, it is not disliked—in fact, it is recommended to remove the distraction. The commentary explains that the reported dislike refers to intentional removal without cause. Killing is permissible, but burying is preferred over throwing. Covering the nose and mouth is prohibited based on a hadith. The passage also addresses the impurity of the louse's shell according to Imam al-Shafi'i, but the Hanafi position is that it is pure, yet throwing it in the mosque is disliked due to general prohibition.

Key Terms
قملة (qamlah): A louse; its taking and killing during prayer is discussed.
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhah tanzīhiyyah): A mild dislike (makruh tanzih) that does not require repetition or compensation.
قشر (qishr): Shell (of the louse); the outer covering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It remains makruh tanzih.
B) It is permissible and not disliked.
C) It is haram.
D) It is wajib to remove it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits removing a distracting louse during prayer, considers its shell and blood pure, and prohibits throwing it in the mosque based on hadith.

Prostrating on the Folds of the Turban: Ruling and Conditions
Ruling on prostrating on folds of turban with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on the folds of a turban, distinguish between valid and invalid prostration based on forehead contact, and cite the evidence.

Core Idea
Prostrating on a turban is valid if the forehead contacts the ground, but disliked without necessity.

This passage addresses a common practice among worshippers: prostrating while wearing a turban with its folds on the forehead. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between a barrier that allows the forehead to feel the ground and one that completely prevents contact. Understanding this distinction ensures your prayer's validity while following the sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is prostrating (sajdah) on the folds (kur) of the turban. The matn initially states it is 'disliked' (makruh) without necessity. Determine the level of dislike.
The commentary clarifies it is tanzihi (mildly disliked), not tahrimi.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
If the fold is on the forehead, it is a barrier that does not prevent contact—valid. If the fold is on the head and the forehead does not touch the ground, the prayer is invalid.
The key is whether the forehead connects to the earth, even through a thin barrier.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Why is it only tanzihi? Because the Prophet himself prostrated on his turban to show permissibility. This becomes evidence for permissibility, so the dislike is light.
The proof (dalil) is the Prophet's action, which is zanni al-thubut usul-wise.
4
Apply to common practice
Many common people place the fold on the head and prostrate without the forehead touching the ground—this is invalid. The ruling thus warns against a widespread mistake.
This is a practical fatwa for today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و يكره السجود على كور (عمامته من غير ضرورة حر أو برد أو خشونة أرض والكور دور من أدوارها بفتح الكاف إذا كان على الجبهة لأنه حائل لا يمنع السجود أما إذا كان على الرأس وسجد عليه ولم تصب جبهته الأرض لا تصح صلاته وكثير من العوام يفعله
قوله: (ويكره السجود على كور عمامته الظاهر أن الكراهة تنزيهية لما نقل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من السجود على كور العمامة تعليماً للجواز، فلم تكن تحريمية كذا في الشرح، ويكره لو فعله لدفع التراب عن وجهه للتكبر، وعن عمامته لا لعدمه كما في سكب الأنهر
And it is disliked to prostrate on the folds of his turban without necessity of heat, cold, or rough ground, and the fold is a round of its rounds, with fat-h on the kaf, if it is on the forehead, because it is a barrier that does not prevent prostration; but if it is on the head and he prostrates on it and his forehead does not touch the ground, his prayer is not valid, and many common people do that. His saying: (it is disliked to prostrate on the folds of his turban) the apparent meaning is that the dislike is tanzihi, due to what has been transmitted that the Prophet prostrated on the folds of his turban to teach permissibility, so it was not tahrimi, as in the Sharh. And it is disliked if he does it to push dust from his face out of arrogance, or from his turban not for its removal, as in Sakan al-Anhur.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on prostrating on the folds of a turban. The matn states it is disliked without a valid excuse like extreme heat, cold, or rough ground. The fold (kur) is the round part of the turban. If the fold is on the forehead, it does not prevent valid prostration (the forehead still touches ground through a barrier that does not prevent contact). However, if the fold is on the head and the person prostrates on it such that the forehead does not touch the ground directly, the prayer is invalid. The commentary clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (mildly disliked) because the Prophet himself prostrated on his turban to show permissibility. Doing so out of arrogance is also disliked. The key distinction is whether the forehead contacts the ground; a thin barrier that allows sensation is acceptable, but a thick one that prevents contact invalidates.

Key Terms
كور العمامة (kūr al-‘amāmah): The folded, round part of a turban.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Always, because it is a barrier.

C) When the fold is on the head and the forehead does not contact the ground.
D) It never invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Prostration on a turban is valid if the forehead contacts the ground, but disliked without necessity; if prevented, prayer invalid.

Prostrating on Images of Living Beings
Ruling on prostrating on a picture of a living being

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on an image of a living being, identify the conditions that affect the degree of dislike, and explain how the general hadith is specified.

Core Idea
Images under feet are fine; images in front or above are disliked—reverence matters.

The matn rules that prostrating on an image of a living being is disliked (makruh) because it resembles worshipping the image. But this broad statement is refined by details about where the image is placed and whether it is habitually humiliated. In this lesson, we unpack the evidence—particularly the hadith of Jibril—and see how later texts classify the intensity of dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states: 'It is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being.' Pinpoint the act (sujud) and the hukm (makruh tanzihi).
The Arabic uses يكره, indicating disapproval but not prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jibril: 'We do not enter a house with a dog or an image.' This suggests that images prevent angels of mercy.
The hadith is cited as evidence for dislike, but then it is specified.
3
Trace the specification (takhsis)
The commentary cites Sahih Ibn Hibban, where the Prophet tells Aisha to cut off heads or turn the curtain into a cushion or carpet. This shows that images that are humiliated (under feet) do not cause dislike.
This specification limits the general hadith to images that are not 'humiliated'.
4
Analyze the degrees of dislike
Al-Nahr ranks: most severe if image in front, then above the head, then behind. If under feet or sat upon, no dislike.
The reasoning: prostrating directly on an image shows magnification; trampling shows disregard.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf on coins
Al-Qadi 'Iyad holds that images on coins do not prevent angels because the hadiths are specified; al-Nawawi holds they do for general meaning. The Hanafi take is the first, as per the mufta bihi.
The recording angels never leave, so the dispute is about angels of mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله: (ويكره السجود على صورة ذي (روح) الأولى ذكر هذا عند ذكر الصورة فيما يأتي، أو يقدّم ما يأتي هنا لجمع الكلام المتناسب، وفي النهر أشدها كراهة أن تكون أمام المصلى، ثم فوق رأسه بحذائه ثم خلفه اهـ فإن قلت كون العلة إمتناع الملائكة .
البيت يقتضي ثبوت الكراهة أيضاً إذا كان التمثال تحت رجليه أو في محل جلوسه، وقد نصوا على أنه لا كراهة في ذلك، وكذا يفيد ثبوتها حديث جبريل إنا لا ندخل بيتاً فيه كلب ولا صورة أجيب عنه بأنه وجد ما يخصصه، وهو ما في صحيح ابن حبان استأذن جبريل عليه السلام على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فقال : ادخل فقال : كيف أدخل، وفي بيتك ستر فيه تصاوير فإن كنت لا بد فاعلاً، فاقطع رؤسها، أو اقطعها وسائد أو اجعلها بساطاً اهـ، وتؤنس بأن هذا يقتضي عدم كراهة الصلاة على بساط فيه تماثيل وإن كانت في موضع سجوده إلا أن يقال ان فيه صورة التشبه بعبادتها حال القيام والركوع وفيه تعظيم لها إن سجد عليها واختلفوا فيما إذا كانت الصورة على دراهم أو دنانير هل تمنع دخول الملائكة، فذهب القاضي عياض إلى عدم المنع ، والأحاديث مخصصة، وذهب النووي إلى المنع للعموم، ثم المراد ملائكة الرحمة لا الحفظة، فإنهم لا يفارقونه إلا عند الجماع والخلاء، وفي شرح المشكاة لمنلا علي : نقلاً . عن الخطابي، وابن الملك أنها لا تدخل بيتاً فيه كلب أو صورة مما يحرم اقتناؤه من الكلاب والصور، وأما ما ليس بحرام من كلب الصيد والزرع والماشية، ومن الصور التي تمتهن في البساط، والوسادة وغيرهما فلا يمنع دخول الملائكة بيته وهذا لا ينافي تحريم التصوير اهـ
And it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being because it resembles worshipping it. His saying: (and it is disliked to prostrate on an image of a living being) it is better to mention this when mentioning the image later, or to present what comes later here to gather the appropriate speech. And in al-Nahr, the most severe dislike is if it is in front of the praying person, then above his head opposite him, then behind him. If you say the reason is the angels' prevention: The house necessitates the establishment of dislike also if the statue is under his feet or in his sitting place, and they have stated that there is no dislike in that. Similarly, the hadith of Jibril establishes it: 'We do not enter a house with a dog or an image.' It was answered that there is something that specifies it, namely what is in Sahih Ibn Hibban: Jibril asked permission, the Prophet said 'Enter,' he said 'How can I enter when in your house there is a curtain with pictures? If you must, then cut off their heads, or cut them into cushions, or make them into a carpet.' This indicates the absence of dislike for praying on a carpet with images, even if they are in the place of prostration, except that it is said it involves resemblance to their worship while standing and bowing, and there is magnification of them if one prostrates on them. They differed on whether images on dirhams or dinars prevent angels from entering; al-Qadi 'Iyad held they do not, as hadiths are specified, and al-Nawawi held they do, due to the general meaning. Then what is meant are the angels of mercy, not the recording angels, for they do not leave him except at intercourse and relieving oneself. And in Sharh al-Mishkat by Mulla Ali, quoting al-Khattabi and Ibn al-Malik, they do not enter a house with a dog or an image that it is prohibited to own; but what is not prohibited, like the hunting dog, farm dog, flock dog, and images that are humiliated in carpets, pillows, etc., do not prevent angels from entering the house, and this does not contradict the prohibition of image-making.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage discusses the dislike of prostrating on an image of a living being. The matn states the reason: resemblance to worshipping the image. The commentary expands on degrees of dislike: worst is when the image is in front of the worshiper, then above the head, then behind. If the image is under the feet or where one sits, there is no dislike. The hadith of Jibril (not entering a house with a dog or image) is specified by another hadith allowing images that are humiliated (as carpets, cushions). The commentator discusses whether images on coins prevent angels of mercy; al-Qadi 'Iyad says no because the hadiths are specified, al-Nawawi says yes for general. The final position depends on whether the image is of a type whose ownership is prohibited. For prayer, the dislike is more related to the direction (qibla side) and the act of prostration on the image, which can be seen as magnification. If the image is trampled, it is not disliked.

Key Terms
صورة ذي روح (ṣūrah dhī rūḥ): An image of a living being (human or animal).
ملائكة الرحمة (malā'ikat al-rahma): Angels of mercy, as opposed to the recording angels (ḥafaẓa).
تمتهن (tumtahan): Humiliated, treated with disregard (e.g., under feet or sat upon).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When it is under the feet.
B) When it is in front of the worshiper.
C) When it is on a dirham.
D) When it is behind the worshiper.

Key Takeaway
Prostration on an image is disliked only when the image is placed in a position of reverence (front/above); images that are humiliated (under feet, sat upon) are not disliked.

The Wajib of Including the Nose in Prostration
Ruling on prostrating without the nose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prostrating without the nose and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the opposite case.

Core Idea
Omitting the nose in sujud is makruh tahrimi because including it is wajib – exception for valid excuse.

Prostration is a fundamental act of prayer, but its exact requirements can be nuanced. The Hanafi school holds that placing both the forehead and the nose on the ground is obligatory (wajib). This lesson examines the ruling when someone prostrates using only the forehead, leaving the nose, and explores the internal disagreement within the Hanafi school on the opposite scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Read the matn and commentary to determine the legal classification (hukm) of leaving the nose during sujud. Note the key phrase: 'makruh tahrimi' because it leaves a wajib.
The ruling is not haram but prohibitively disliked.
2
Understand the Basis: Wajib or Sunnah?
The text explicitly states that including the nose is wajib. Distinguish this from rukn (pillar). Omission of wajib requires sujud al-sahw; omission of rukn invalidates the act.
Hanafi usul: wajib is proven by zanni dalil.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa says the opposite (only nose, no forehead) is also makruh tahrimi. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prohibit it unless the forehead has an excuse. Compare the stances.
The mufta bihi is to include both; the Sahibayn's view is stricter for the forehead.
4
Apply the Exception for Excuse
The commentary notes that if there is an excuse (e.g., bandage, injury), the ruling changes. The omission becomes permissible and no sujud al-sahw is required.
The phrase 'bila 'udhr' restricts the karahah.
5
Contrast with Other Madhahib
The Shafi'i school considers the nose sunnah, not wajib. Recognize the practical difference: no sujud al-sahw required in Shafi'i school for omitting the nose.
This highlights the binding force of Hanafi wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و يكره الاقتصار على الجبهة في السجود (بلا عذر بالأنف لترك واجب ضم الأنف تحريماً
قوله : ويكره الاقتصار الخ) وكذا عكسه عند الإمام ومنعه الصاحبان إلا إذا كان بالجبهة عذر أفاده السيد. قوله: (تحريماً) أي كراهة تحريم، ويفيده قوله لترك واجب ضم الأنف
And it is disliked to restrict prostration to the forehead without an excuse from the nose, because it leaves the obligatory (wajib) of including the nose, with prohibition (tahrimi). His saying: (and it is disliked to restrict ...) and also the opposite according to Imam, and the two companions prohibited it except if there is an excuse of the forehead, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: (with prohibition) meaning makruh tahrimi, and it is indicated by his saying 'because it leaves the wajib of including the nose.'
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on prostrating with only the forehead, excluding the nose. The matn states it is dislikedit is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because including the nose in prostration is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. The commentary notes that the opposite (prostrating with only the nose, excluding the forehead) is also disliked according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prohibit it unless there is an excuse for the forehead. The key point: prostration requires both forehead and nose; omitting any part without excuse is makruh tahrimi. The ruling emphasizes the Hanafi position that the nose is a wajib part of prostration, not just sunnah.

Key Terms
واجب ضم الأنف (wājib ḍamm al-anf): The obligatory inclusion of the nose in prostration along with the forehead.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is haram and invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Prostration requires both forehead and nose; omitting the nose without excuse is makruh tahrimi and requires sujud al-sahw.

Rulings on Prayer in Road, Bathroom, and Cemetery
Ruling with proof on disliked places for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four places where prayer is disliked in the Hanafi school and explain the reasons for each.

Core Idea
Prayer is disliked in places that violate public rights or resemble practices of disbelievers.

The Hanafi school teaches that while prayer is valid in most locations, certain places carry a degree of dislike (karahah). This lesson unpacks the rulings for praying in the road, bathroom, latrine, and cemetery, exploring the different reasons behind the dislike and the intra-madhhab differences on the bathroom's cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four locations and their hukm
The text explicitly lists: road (ṭarīq), bathroom (ḥammām), latrine (makhraj), and cemetery (maqbara). All are makruh to pray in, with variations in severity.
Makruh tanzih for road and bathroom; cemetery may be makruh tahrimi.
2
Examine the rationale for each
Road: because it occupies the public right of way and distracts from khushu. Bathroom: two opinions – removal of impurities or abode of devils. Latrine: similar to bathroom. Cemetery: resembles Jews/Christians who pray at graves.
The hadith about Iblis is cited for the devil abode theory.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the bathroom
If the cause is impurity removal, then washing the spot removes the dislike. If the cause is devils, then dislike remains even if washed. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is always disliked.
This ikhtilaf affects practical fatwa.
4
Apply the exception for prophets' graves
Prayer in a prophets' grave area is not disliked because prophets are alive in their graves. However, one should not pray facing the grave directly.
Example: the resting place of Isma'il (AS) in the Hijr.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
Some Shafi'is allow prayer in a bathroom if the spot is clean. The Hanafi position is more cautious, emphasizing the hadith of Iblis.

Source Text

و تكره الصلاة في الطريق لشغله حق العامة ومنعهم من المرور (و) في (الحمام وفي المخرج) أي الكثيف (و) تكره الصلاة (في المقبرة) وأمثالها لأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى أن
قوله: (شغله حق العامة) والشغل البال عن الخشوع، فيشتغل بالخلق عن الحق، وعن هذا شرط بعضهم أن يكون في العمران لا في البرية أفاده شارح المشكاة. قوله : (وفي الحمام) مأخوذ من الحميم، وهو الماء الحار وكذا المغتسل واختلف في العلة فقيل: لأن كلا منهما محل إزالة النجاسات، ومصب الغسلات فعلى هذا لو غسل موضعاً في الحمام لا يكره ومشى عليه قاضيخان و به جزم الكمال في زاد الفقير وقيل العلة كونه مأوى الشياطين، فقد روى أن أبليس لما هبط إلى الأرض قال يا رب اجعل لي بيتاً . قال :الحمام قال: اجعل لي مقعداً قال : الأسواق قال : اجعل لي قرناء قال الشعراء قال: اجعل لي كتاباً قال : الوشم: ويتفرع على هذا أن الصلاة تكره داخل الحمام سواء غسل ذلك الموضع أم لا . قوله: (وفي المقبرة) بتثليث الباء لأنه تشبه باليهود والنصارى . قال : العنة الله على اليهود والنصارى اتخذوا قبور أنبيائهم مساجد وسواء كانت فوقه أو خلفه، أو تحت ما هو واقف عليه، ويستثنى مقابر الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام فلا تكره الصلاة فيها مطلقاً منبوشة، أو لا بعد أن لا يكون القبر في جهة القبلة لأنهم أحياء في قبورهم ألا ترى أن مرقد اسمعيل عليه السلام في الحجر تحت الميزاب
And prayer is disliked in the road because it occupies the right of the public and prevents them from passing, and in the bathroom and in the latrine, i.e., the thick place, and prayer is disliked in the cemetery and similar places because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade that. His saying: (occupies the right of the public) and the occupation busies the mind from humility, so one becomes occupied with creation instead of the Creator. And based on this, some conditioned that it should be in the inhabited area, not in the wilderness, as mentioned by the commentator of al-Mishkat. His saying: (in the bathroom) derived from hamim, which is hot water, and likewise the washroom. There is disagreement about the cause: some say because each of them is a place for removing impurities and a drain for washings; on this basis, if one washes a spot in the bathroom, it is not disliked, and Qadi Khan acted on it, and al-Kamal affirmed it in Zad al-Faqir. Others say the cause is that it is a dwelling for devils; it is narrated that Iblis when he descended to earth said, 'O Lord, make a house for me.' He said: 'The bathroom.' He said: 'Make a sitting place for me.' He said: 'The markets.' He said: 'Make companions for me.' He said: 'The poets.' He said: 'Make a book for me.' He said: 'Tattooing.' And it branches from this that prayer is disliked inside the bathroom whether that spot is washed or not. His saying: (in the cemetery) with three ways of pronouncing the ba, because it resembles the Jews and Christians. He said: 'May Allah curse the Jews and Christians, they took the graves of their prophets as places of worship.' And whether it is above him or behind him or under what he is standing on. And an exception is made for the graves of the prophets, peace be upon them, so prayer is not disliked in their graves at all, whether the grave is dug up or not, provided that the grave is not in the direction of the qibla, because they are alive in their graves; do you not see that the resting place of Isma'il (peace be upon him) is in the Hijr under the waterspout?
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage lists several places where prayer is disliked (makruh). The road: because it disrupts public passage and distracts from khushu. The condition is that it be in a populated area, not wilderness. The bathroom (hamam) and latrine: the reason is either because they are places of impurity removal or because they are abodes of devils. According to the first view, if the spot is washed clean, prayer is not disliked; according to the second, it is always disliked. The relied-upon view (mashaykha) is that it is disliked. The cemetery: prayer is disliked because it resembles the practice of Jews and Christians who pray at graves. The prohibition includes praying on, behind, or under a grave. Exception: the graves of prophets; prayer there is not disliked because prophets are alive in their graves. Additionally, if the grave is in front of the qibla direction, it is disliked to pray towards it.

Key Terms
حق العامة (ḥaqq al-‘āmmah): The right of the public to use the road; praying in it obstructs this right.
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike; acts are valid but discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is prayer disliked in a cemetery according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the ground is impure.
B) Because it resembles the practice of Jews and Christians.
C) Because it disturbs the dead.
D) Because angels do not enter cemeteries.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in road, bathroom, latrine, and cemetery is disliked for different reasons, but the Hanafi school emphasizes public rights and distinctiveness from non-Muslim practices.

Makruh Acts in Prayer: Land, Garments, and Suppressing Needs
Rulings on prayer in another's land, specific garment cases, and suppressing bodily needs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in another's land without permission, in a usurped or silk garment, and while suppressing needs, and identify the exception for fear of missing the time.

Core Idea
Prayer in these situations is valid but disliked; suppressing needs is makruh, not invalid, unless time is short.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi continues the critical refinement of disliked acts in prayer. He addresses three additional scenarios: praying on land without permission, in certain garments, and while suppressing bodily needs. The Hanafi school holds that these acts are valid but makruh tanzih (disliked), with the exception of extreme time constraints. The passage also includes a cross-madhhab dispute with the Zahiri school regarding the validity of prayer while suppressing needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify Each Act and Its Ruling
List the three main scenarios: (1) prayer in another's land without permission, (2) prayer in a usurped or silk garment, (3) prayer while suppressing urine, stool, or wind. For each, state the Hanafi hukm: makruh tanzih (disliked).
The dislike for land depends on owner type and relationship.
2
Locate the Proof for Suppressing Needs
The dalil for the ruling on suppressing needs is the hadith: 'It is not permissible for anyone who believes in Allah and the Last Day to pray while retaining urine until he relieves himself.' The Hanafi school interprets 'لا يحل' as indicating dislike (karahah) rather than prohibition (haram), citing other evidence.
The Zahiri school takes the apparent meaning as prohibition, making the prayer invalid.
3
Understand the Rational Cause
The rational cause (illa ma'qula) for dislike is the disturbance of mind and loss of khushu' (concentration) that results from suppressing the need. This cause unites urine, stool, and wind.
The cause is rational, not purely textual.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
The Zahiri school holds that prayer while suppressing needs is invalid (batil), based on the apparent meaning of the hadith. The Hanafi school responds that the hadith indicates dislike, not invalidity, and that the prayer is valid but deficient.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Apply the Exception for Time Constraint
If a person fears that the prayer time will expire if he relieves himself and makes wudu, he should pray in his current state (with dislike) rather than miss the prayer. This is applying the principle of choosing the lesser of two evils.
This exception overrides the general dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وتكره في أرض الغير بلا رضاه) بأن كانت لذمي مطلقاً لأنه يأبى، أو لمسلم وهي مزروعة أو مكروبة، ولم يكن بينهما صداقة، ولا مودة، أو كان صاحبها سيء الخلق، ولو كان في بيت إنسان الأحسن أن يستأذنه، وإلا فلا بأس كما في الفتح، وفي مختارات الفتاوى الصلاة في أرض مغصوبة جائزة ولكن يعاقب بظلمه فما كان بينه وبين العباد يعاقب كما في الفتاوى الهندية قوله : (صلى فيها) لأن الظاهر يرضى بها لأنه ينال أجراً من غير اكتساب منه، ولا أذن في الطريق لأنه حق المسلم، والكافر كذا في الشرح قوله صلى في الطريق) لأنه لا يرضى بها كذا في البرهان، والطريق ليست للكافر على الخصوص كذا في الشرح . فروع: تكره الصلاة في الثوب المغصوب وإن لم يجد غيره لعدم جواز الإنتفاع بملك الغير قبل الأذن، أو أداء الضمان وتكره في الثوب الحرير إلا إذا لم يجد غيره إذ كل منهما حق الله تعالى. والصلاة في الثوب الحرير أخف منها عرياناً، ولا تكره على الحرير. قوله : ومدافعاً لأحد الأخبثين) علة الكراهة المعقولة ما يحصل من تشويش البال، وشغل الخاطر لأجل قضاء الحاجة المخل بالخشوع وقالت الظاهرية : إنها لا تصح أخذاً بظاهر الحديث . قوله: (ولو حدث فيها الخ وحينئذ فيقطع ويتخفف ويستأنف . قوله : (وهو حاقن من الحقن، وهو حبس البول كما ذكره العلامة نوح، والمراد ما هو أعم من البول، والغائط والريح لاتحاد العلة. قوله : (تقدم بيانها وهو ما دون ربع الثوب في المخففة، وقدر الدرهم في المغلظة . قوله : (خروجاً من (الخلاف) هذا إنما يظهر علة للقطع لا للكراهة . قوله : (إلا إذا خاف فوت الوقت ظاهره أنها تنتفي الكراهة عند ذلك، والذي يفيده كلام غيره الكراهة وارتكابها حينئذ من ارتكاب أخف الضررين والذي في الزيلعي ينبغي إذا كان في الوقت سعة أما إذا ضاق بحيث تفوته الصلاة إذا تخفف وتوضأ فإنه يصلي بهذه الحالة لأن الأداء الكراهة أولى مع القضاء اهـ بالمعنى، وحكى أبو سعيد أنه يتخفف، من
He said: And prayer in the land of another without his permission is disliked. If it belongs to a dhimmi absolutely because he would refuse, or to a Muslim and it is cultivated or planted, and there is no friendship or affection between them, or the owner is ill-tempered. And if it is in a person's house, it is better to seek his permission; otherwise there is no harm, as in al-Fath. In Mukhtarat al-Fatawa: Prayer in usurped land is permissible, but one is punished for his oppression; whatever is between him and the people, he will be punished, as in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya. His statement: (He prays in it) because apparently he is pleased with it because he obtains reward without any effort from him. And he does not give permission in the road because it is the right of the Muslim, and the disbeliever is like that in the commentary. His statement: (He prays in the road) because he is not pleased with it, as in al-Burhan. And the road is not specifically for the disbeliever, as in the commentary. Branches: Prayer in a usurped garment is disliked even if he does not find another, due to the impermissibility of benefiting from another's property without permission or payment of compensation. And prayer in a silk garment is disliked unless he does not find another, since each of them is a right of Allah. Prayer in a silk garment is lighter than being naked, and it is not disliked on silk. His statement: (While suppressing one of the two impurities) the rational cause of dislike is what arises from disturbance of mind and occupation of thought for the sake of relieving oneself, which is detrimental to khushu'. The Zahiri school said: It is not valid, taking the apparent meaning of the hadith. His statement: (Even if it occurs during it) and then he should cut off and relieve himself and recommence. His statement: (He is haqin) from haqn, which is retention of urine as mentioned by al-Allama Nuh. What is meant is general, including urine, stool, and wind due to the unity of the cause. His statement: (Its explanation has preceded) which is less than a quarter of the garment in light impurity, and the amount of a dirham in heavy impurity. His statement: (Out of disagreement) this only appears as a cause for cutting, not for dislike. His statement: (Except if he fears the passing of the time) apparently the dislike is negated in that case. What the speech of others indicates is dislike, and committing it then is committing the lesser of two evils. What is in al-Zayla'i: If there is an abundance of time, then if it is narrow such that the prayer would be missed if he relieves himself and makes wudu, then he prays in this state, because performing with dislike is better than qada'. A similar meaning. Abu Sa'id narrated that he should relieve himself.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage continues the critical refinement, covering additional situations where prayer is disliked. It first discusses prayer in another person's land without permission. The ruling depends on the owner: if dhimmi, always disliked; if Muslim, disliked if the land is cultivated or there is no friendship. In a house, permission should be sought. Prayer in a usurped land is valid but sinful. Branches include prayer in a usurped garment (disliked) and a silk garment (disliked unless no other). Then the passage covers praying while suppressing urine, stool, or wind. The cause is distraction from khushu'. The Zahiri school considers it invalid, but Hanafi says it is makruh. If it occurs during prayer, one should cut off, relieve, and restart. The exception is fear of missing the time: then it is better to pray with dislike than to miss the prayer, as it is the lesser of two evils. This follows the author's order: first the land ruling, then branches, then suppressing needs, then the exception for time.

Key Terms
أرض الغير (ard al-ghayr): Land belonging to another person; prayer in it without permission is disliked.
مدافعاً لأحد الأخبثين (mudafi'an li-ahad al-akhbatayn): Suppressing one of the two impurities (urine or stool) while praying; it is disliked due to distraction.
حاقن (haqin): One who is retaining urine; the ruling applies to stool and wind as well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He should continue but his prayer is invalid.
D) He may stop and then continue from where he left off.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in these situations is valid but disliked; in time constraint, pray with dislike rather than miss the prayer.

Rulings on Praying in Usurped or Silk Garments
Two rulings on garment conditions for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on praying in a usurped garment and in a silk garment, and explain the reasoning behind each ruling.

Core Idea
Prayer in a usurped garment is valid but sinful; prayer in silk is disliked but permissible in necessity.

This passage presents two derivative rulings (furuʿ) concerning the garment worn during prayer. The first addresses a garment that has been taken unjustly (ghasb), and the second addresses pure silk. These rulings demonstrate how the Hanafi school balances the validity of prayer with the prohibition of sinful acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and identify the two specific garments discussed: the usurped garment and the silk garment.
These are distinct rulings with different underlying reasons.
2
State the ruling for each case
For each garment, determine the legal ruling (hukm) according to the passage. Note that both are described as 'makruh' disliked.
Usurped garment: makruh tahrimi (close to haram). Silk: makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), but exception exists.
3
Understand the reasoning
Identify why each garment is disliked. For usurped: it involves using another's property without permission. For silk: it is a luxury forbidden to men, but the prayer itself is valid.
The reasoning is based on the prohibition of benefiting from others' property without consent and the general prohibition of silk for men.
4
Note the exceptions
The passage states two exceptions: (1) if the person has no other garment, the dislike for silk is lifted; (2) praying on silk (e.g., a silk mat) is not disliked. Also, for usurped, the dislike remains even if no other garment, but the prayer is valid.
The exception for silk shows the priority of covering the nakedness over avoiding the disliked material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع: تكره الصلاة في الثوب المغصوب وإن لم يجد غيره لعدم جواز الإنتفاع بملك الغير قبل الأذن، أو أداء الضمان وتكره في الثوب الحرير إلا إذا لم يجد غيره إذ كل منهما حق الله تعالى. والصلاة في الثوب الحرير أخف منها عرياناً، ولا تكره على الحرير.
Branches: It is disliked to pray in a usurped garment even if one does not find another, because utilizing another's property is not permissible before permission or payment of compensation. And it is disliked to pray in a silk garment unless one does not find another, because each is a right of Allah. And praying in a silk garment is lighter than praying naked. And it is not disliked to pray on silk.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This short passage lists two derivative rulings (furu') related to the garment used in prayer: First, it is makruh to pray in a garment that has been usurped (ghasb), even if the person has no other clothing. This is because it is not permissible to benefit from another's property without permission or payment of compensation. Second, it is makruh to pray in a pure silk garment for men, unless one cannot find any other covering; in that case, it is permissible. The text notes that prayer in silk is less severe than praying completely naked, and it is not disliked to pray on a silk surface (such as a prayer mat made of silk), as the prohibition is about wearing silk, not using it as a place.

Key Terms
ثوب مغصوب (thawb maghsud): A garment that has been taken unjustly from its owner without permission; using it in prayer is disliked.
ثوب حرير (thawb harir): Silk garment; wearing it in prayer for men is disliked unless necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is prohibited (haram) absolutely.
D) It is recommended (mustahab) because silk is pure.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in a usurped or silk garment is valid but disliked; necessity lifts the dislike for silk.
