Ruling on Praying While Needing to Relieve Oneself
Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying while needing to relieve oneself, explain the Hanafi interpretation of the relevant hadith, and apply the exception for fear of missing the prayer time or congregation.

Core Idea
Praying while needing relief is valid but disliked; only cut if time permits and no risk of missing fard.

This lesson addresses a common situation: needing to urinate, defecate, or pass wind while about to pray or during prayer. The Hanafi school rules it makruh tanzihi (disliked but valid), while the Zahiriyya school deems the prayer invalid. We will examine the textual evidence, the rational cause, and the exceptions that allow continuing the prayer when time or congregation is at stake.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its rational cause
From the text: 'مدافعاً لأحد الأخبثين' – the cause of dislike is the disturbance of mind and lack of khushu'. Understand that the ruling is makruh tanzihi, not haram or invalid.
The term 'حاقن' covers urine, stool, and wind due to shared cause.
2
Examine the Zahiri objection
The Zahiriyya take the hadith 'لا يحل...' literally and conclude the prayer is invalid. Identify their proof and the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
Hanafis interpret 'لا يحل' as prohibition of initiating prayer, not invalidation of the act itself.
3
Understand the exception for fear of missing time or congregation
Al-Tahtawi explains that if one fears missing the prayer time or the congregation (which is wajib or emphasized), he should pray despite the need, as committing the lesser harm (disliked act) is better than missing the greater obligation.
Reference to al-Zayla'i and al-Khulasa for congregation scenarios.
4
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Given ample time: it is mustahabb to cut, relieve, and restart. Given tight time or no alternative congregation: continue praying; the prayer is valid but disliked.
The exception covers both time and congregation; if finding another congregation is possible, cut is still recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ومدافعاً لأحد الأخبثين) علة الكراهة المعقولة ما يحصل من تشويش البال، وشغل الخاطر لأجل قضاء الحاجة المخل بالخشوع وقالت الظاهرية : إنها لا تصح أخذاً بظاهر الحديث . قوله: (ولو حدث فيها الخ وحينئذ فيقطع ويتخفف ويستأنف . قوله : (وهو حاقن من الحقن، وهو حبس البول كما ذكره العلامة نوح، والمراد ما هو أعم من البول، والغائط والريح لاتحاد العلة. قوله : (تقدم بيانها وهو ما دون ربع الثوب في المخففة، وقدر الدرهم في المغلظة . قوله : (خروجاً من (الخلاف) هذا إنما يظهر علة للقطع لا للكراهة . قوله : (إلا إذا خاف فوت الوقت ظاهره أنها تنتفي الكراهة عند ذلك، والذي يفيده كلام غيره الكراهة وارتكابها حينئذ من ارتكاب أخف الضررين والذي في الزيلعي ينبغي إذا كان في الوقت سعة أما إذا ضاق بحيث تفوته الصلاة إذا تخفف وتوضأ فإنه يصلي بهذه الحالة لأن الأداء الكراهة أولى مع القضاء اهـ بالمعنى، وحكى أبو سعيد أنه يتخفف، من (الجماعة) فحينئذ يصلي بتلك الحال لأنّ إخراج الصلاة عن وقتها حرام والجماعة مؤكدة أو واجبة (وإلا) أي وإن لم يخف القوت ندب قطعها وقضية قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا يحل وجوب القطع للإكمال قوله : (أو قوت الجماعة) قال في الخلاصة إن كان بحال تفوته الجماعة فإن كان بحال يجد جماعة أخرى فإنه يقطع الصلاة، ويغسل وإن كان لا يجد أو خاف خروج الوقت يمضي على صلاته اهـ. قوله : فلا يفوته يوجد هنا في بعض النسخ زيادة ونصها، وقد ظهر أن الاستثناء يرجع إلى المسئلتين قبله أه.
His statement: 'and while defending against one of the two filths' – the rational cause of dislike is the disturbance of mind and preoccupation of thought due to the need to relieve oneself, which harms humility. And the Zahiriyya said: it is not valid, taking the apparent meaning of the hadith. His statement: 'and if it occurs during it' – then he cuts off, relieves himself, and begins anew. His statement: 'he is haqin' from al-haqn, which is holding back urine, as mentioned by Allamah Nuh, and the meaning is inclusive of urine, stool, and wind due to the unification of cause. His statement: 'its explanation has preceded' – which is less than a quarter of the garment in the case of light impurity, and the size of a dirham in heavy impurity. His statement: 'to exit from disagreement' – this only appears as a cause for cutting, not for dislike. His statement: 'except if he fears missing the time' – apparently dislike is negated then, and what benefits from the speech of others is that there is dislike and committing it then is committing the lesser of two harms. What is in al-Zayla'i: it is appropriate if there is ample time, but if it is so tight that he would miss the prayer if he relieves and performs wudu, then he prays in that state because performing with dislike is better than making it up. He said with meaning, and Abu Sa'id narrated that he relieves himself from (the congregation) – then he prays in that state because taking the prayer out of its time is haram, and congregation is emphasized or obligatory. (Otherwise), i.e., if he does not fear missing, then it is recommended to cut it off. And the purport of his statement, peace be upon him: 'It is not permissible' necessitates obligation of cutting for completion. His statement: 'or fear of losing the congregation' – al-Khulasa said: If it is such that he will miss the congregation, then if he can find another congregation, he cuts off the prayer and washes; if he cannot find or fears loss of time, he continues his prayer. End. His statement: 'so he does not miss it' – here in some copies there is an addition: 'and it has become apparent that the exception refers to the two preceding issues.' End.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya discusses the ruling on praying while needing to relieve oneself (urine, stool, or wind). The matn states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray while 'defending against one of the two filths' or wind, and if it occurs during prayer, one should cut the prayer, relieve himself, and restart. The commentary provides the reason for dislike: it disturbs the mind and harms khushu' (humility). It then mentions the view of the Zahiriyya (a school that follows literal meanings) that such prayer is invalid based on the hadith. The Hanafi position, however, is that it is disliked but not invalid, and the hadith is interpreted to mean that one should not begin prayer in that state. The commentary then clarifies the term 'haqin' (holding back urine) and that the ruling applies to all three. It then discusses the exception: if one fears missing the prayer time or the congregation, he should pray despite the need, because committing a disliked act is better than missing the obligatory time or congregation (which is either emphasized sunnah or wajib). The ruling on cutting: if there is ample time, it is recommended to cut, but if time is tight, one continues. The commentary also references al-Zayla'i and al-Khulasa for the congregation aspect.

Key Terms
مدافع لأحد الأخبثين (mudafi' li-ahad al-akhbathayn): The state of needing to expel urine or stool (the two filths); also includes wind.
حاقن (haqin): One who is holding back urine; used generally for any need to relieve.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of the hadith 'لا يحل لأحد يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر أن يصلي وهو حاقن'?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) It is disliked to begin prayer in that state.
C) The prayer is prohibited and must be repeated.
D) The hadith only applies to urine, not stool or wind.

Key Takeaway
Praying while needing to relieve oneself is valid but disliked; the prayer should be cut only if there is ample time; otherwise, continue to preserve the prayer time or congregation.

Disliked Conditions in Prayer: Clothes, Head Cover, Food Presence
Lists three disliked conditions in prayer with proofs and clarifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in ordinary clothes, with uncovered head, and in the presence of food, and explain the proof and the distinction between tanzihi and tahrimi dislike.

Core Idea
Prayer with ordinary clothes, uncovered head out of laziness, or when food is desired is valid but disliked — because these distract from khushu'.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies three situations that are disliked (makruh) in prayer but do not invalidate it. The key is understanding the level of dislike (tanzihi), the role of intention (laziness vs. disrespect), and the interpretation of the hadith 'La salata bi-hadrati ta'am'.

Guided Path
1
Identify each disliked act and its ruling level
List the three acts: praying in ordinary clothes (thiyab al-badhlah), praying with uncovered head due to laziness (makshuf al-ra's takasulan), and praying when food is present and desired (bi-hadrati ta'am yamilu tab'uhu ilayhi). Note that each is makruh tanzihi (prophylactic dislike).
Makruh tanzihi means it is better to avoid but the prayer is valid.
2
Distinguish intention: laziness vs. disrespect, desire vs. no desire
For uncovered head: if done out of laziness, it is disliked; if out of disrespect (istikhfaf), it could lead to kufr. For food: dislike applies only if one's nature inclines to eat it. If one does not desire it, there is no dislike.
The same act can change ruling based on intention (qasd).
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The hadith: 'La salata bi-hadrati ta'am wa la huwa yudafi'uhu al-akhbathan' (No prayer in the presence of food nor while defending against the two filths). Also, the statement of Umar: 'Allah is more deserving that you adorn yourself for Him.'
These are ahad hadith, zanni in thubut and dalala.
4
Interpret the proof: 'la salata' means incomplete prayer, not invalidation
Hanafi scholars interpret 'la salata' as 'no complete prayer' (due to lack of khushu'), not that the prayer is invalid. This is supported by the context of distraction.
The ruling is makruh tanzihi, not haram or batil.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position is that these conditions are makruh tanzihi. Prayer performed thus is valid but deficient in perfection. The worshipper should avoid them and strive for khushu'.
This is the view of al-Tahtawi and the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وتكره الصلاة في ثياب البذلة الظاهر أن الكراهة للتنزيه كما في البحر، وفي القهستاني : إن الكراهة للفعل في هذه الأشياء أي إيقاع الصلاة فيها إلا الصلاة وفي الجلابي أنها تكره بسبب هذه الأفعال اهـ. قوله : (تكاسلاً) وإن فعله استخفافاً كفر نعوذ بالله الحفيظ أفاده الشرح . قوله : (ويستحب له ذلك) به علم رد قول من قال : إنه عنده قصد ذلك خلاف الأولى. قوله: (وعن علي الخ) مما يؤيد الأول كما ان قوله : وعن جماعة وقول البغوي يؤيد الثاني قوله: (وتكره بحضرة طعام أي مباح أما إذا كان للغير، ولم يأذن له لا تنكره أقول الظاهر أن عليه أن يتباعد عنه قوله : (يميل طبعه إليه أما إذا كان لا يميل إليه فلا كراهة والحكم في قطعها عند ذلك كالحكم إذا صلى حاملاً نجاسة قليلة قوله : (لا صلاة بحضرة طعام) أي لا صلاة كاملة بحضرة الطعام الذي يريد المصلى أكله كذا في الشرح قوله: (محمول على تأخيرها عن وقتها)
His statement: 'And it is disliked to pray in ordinary clothes' – apparently the dislike is tanzihi (prophylactic) as in al-Bahr. And in al-Qahistani: the dislike is for the act in these things, i.e., performing prayer in them, except prayer itself. And in al-Jilabi: it is disliked due to these actions. End. His statement: 'out of laziness' – and if he does it out of disrespect, he disbelieves; may Allah protect us, as in al-Sharh. His statement: 'and it is recommended for him to do that' – by this is refuted the statement of those who said that if he intends that, it is contrary to the better. His statement: 'and from Ali, etc.' – this supports the first, just as his statement: 'and from a group' and the statement of al-Baghawi supports the second. His statement: 'and it is disliked in the presence of food' – i.e., permissible food; but if it belongs to someone else and he did not permit him, then it is not disliked? I say: it is apparent that he should distance himself from it. His statement: 'his nature inclines to it' – but if he does not incline to it, then there is no dislike. And the ruling of cutting it then is like the ruling if he prays carrying a small amount of impurity. His statement: 'No prayer in the presence of food' – i.e., no complete prayer in the presence of food that the worshipper intends to eat, as in al-Sharh. His statement: 'is interpreted as delaying it from its time.'
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage discusses three disliked matters in prayer: wearing ordinary working clothes, praying with the head uncovered out of laziness, and praying when food is present and one desires it. The commentator first clarifies that the dislike for praying in 'thiyab al-badhlah' (ordinary or humble clothes) is tanzihi (prophylactic dislike), meaning it is better avoided but not sinful. However, if one does so out of disrespect (istikhfaf), it could lead to disbelief. He then mentions that it is mustahab (recommended) to wear better clothes for prayer. Regarding the head being uncovered, the text distinguishes between doing so out of laziness (disliked) and doing so as a sign of humility and supplication (permissible, even recommended). The commentator cites differences among scholars on khushu' (humility) and notes that some sahaba associated khushu' with stillness in prayer. Finally, the passage addresses praying when food is present and one desires it: it is disliked because it distracts from khushu', based on the hadith 'La salata bi-hadrati ta'am' (No prayer in the presence of food), which is interpreted to mean no complete prayer, not that the prayer is invalid. If one does not desire the food, there is no dislike. If the food belongs to others and they have not permitted, one should distance oneself. The ruling on cutting the prayer in this situation is compared to that of praying with a small amount of impurity.

Key Terms
ثياب البذلة (thiyab al-badhlah): Ordinary, everyday clothes that are not kept clean from dirt or are shameful; it is disliked to pray in them.
مكشوف الرأس (makshuf al-ra's): Uncovered head; if done out of laziness, it is disliked, but if done for humility, it is permitted and even recommended.
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Prophylactic dislike; act is better avoided but not sinful; prayer is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it not disliked to pray in the presence of food?
A) When the food is permissible.
B) When the food belongs to someone else and they have not permitted.
C) When the worshipper does not have an inclination toward the food.
D) When the prayer is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Prayer in ordinary clothes, with uncovered head out of laziness, or when food is desired is makruh tanzihi — valid but deficient in khushu' — and the hadith 'La salata' is interpreted as no complete prayer, not invalidation.

Prayer in the Presence of Food: Understanding the Hanafi Ruling
Explanation of the ruling on praying while food is served and desired

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying when food is present, explain the dalil and its interpretation, and apply the conditions for the dislike (karahah).

Core Idea
The presence of desired food while praying renders the prayer incomplete, not invalid — the ruling is makruh tanzih.

You may have heard the hadith 'There is no prayer in the presence of food.' Does this mean your prayer is invalid if you pray while your meal is waiting? The Hanafi school, through careful analysis of the hadith, distinguishes between a complete and a valid prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the practical guidance for the believer who values khushu (focus) in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm is. Here: praying while food is present and one desires it → makruh tanzih (disliked, not prohibited).
The karahah is tanzihi, meaning the prayer is valid but deficient in completeness.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith from Muslim: 'La salata bi hadrati ta'am' (no prayer in the presence of food). Also the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim instructing to start with dinner if it is served.
The dalil is an ahad hadith, so it yields zanni thubut and dalalah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation of 'la salata'
Hanafis interpret the negation as referring to completeness (kaamilah), not validity. This is supported by context and other narrations that recommend eating first for khushu.
The phrase 'la salata' does not nullify the obligation; it indicates imperfection.
4
List the conditions for the ruling
The dislike applies only when: (1) the food is permissible (halal), (2) the person genuinely desires it (nature inclines), (3) the food is present and ready, and (4) it is not someone else's property without permission.
If the food is not desired or is impermissible, there is no karahah.
5
Understand the recommended action
If one has not yet started prayer, it is recommended to eat first and then pray to ensure khushu. If already in prayer, it is recommended to cut the prayer, eat, and then repeat the prayer (if time allows).
Cutting the prayer is permissible (makruh tanzih to continue) and is better for achieving khushu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و تكره بحضرة طعام يميل طبعه إليه لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : الا صلاة بحضرة طعام ولا هو يدافعه الأخبثان، رواه مسلم وما في أبي داود لا تؤخر الصلاة لطعام، ولا لغيره محمول على تأخيرها عن وقتها لصريح ويستحب ويتوضأ وإن خرج الوقت لأن المقصود من الصلاة الخشوع (۱) فلا يفوته . قوله : (و تكره بحضرة طعام أي مباح أما إذا كان للغير، ولم يأذن له لا تنكره أقول الظاهر أن عليه أن يتباعد عنه قوله : (يميل طبعه إليه أما إذا كان لا يميل إليه فلا كراهة والحكم في قطعها عند ذلك كالحكم إذا صلى حاملاً نجاسة قليلة قوله : (لا صلاة بحضرة طعام) أي لا صلاة كاملة بحضرة الطعام الذي يريد المصلى أكله كذا في الشرح قوله: (محمول على تأخيرها عن وقتها) قوله : (إذا وضع عشاء أحدكم وأقيمت الصلاة فابدوا بالعشاء ولا تعجل حتى يفرغ منه) رواه الشيخان وإنما أمر بتقديمه لئلا يذهب الخشوع باشتغال فكره به
And it is disliked to pray in the presence of food to which one's nature inclines, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'There is no prayer in the presence of food, nor while one is resisting the two filths.' Narrated by Muslim. And what is in Abu Dawud: 'Do not delay prayer for food or anything else' is interpreted as delaying it beyond its time due to the explicit text... And it is recommended that he performs wudu even if the time has passed, because the purpose of prayer is khushu so that he does not miss it. His statement: (Disliked in the presence of food) means permissible food; if it belongs to someone else and he has not permitted him, it is not disliked? I say: the apparent view is that he should move away from it. His statement: (to which his nature inclines) if he does not incline to it, then there is no dislike. And the ruling on cutting it (prayer) in that case is like the ruling when one prays carrying a small impurity. His statement: ('There is no prayer in the presence of food') means no complete prayer in the presence of food that the worshipper intends to eat, as in the Sharh. His statement: (Interpreted as delaying it beyond its time) His statement: ('When the evening meal of any of you is served and the prayer is commenced, start with the evening meal and do not hasten until you finish it') narrated by the two Shaykhs. He commanded to prioritize it so that khushu does not go away due to occupation of the mind with it.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on praying when food is present and one desires it. The source text (Maraqi al-Falah) states it is makruh (disliked) based on the hadith from Muslim: 'There is no prayer in the presence of food, nor while one is resisting the two filths (urine and stool).' The commentator clarifies that the karahah is tanzihi (close to permissible) and applies only to permissible food that one genuinely desires. If the food belongs to another without permission, the worshipper should move away. The hadith from Abu Dawud ('Do not delay prayer for food') is interpreted as referring to delaying prayer beyond its time, not to delaying it for food. The well-known hadith from Bukhari and Muslim about not rushing to pray when dinner is served emphasizes that if the evening meal is ready, one should eat first to ensure khushu (focus) in prayer. The commentary also notes that if one starts prayer despite food being present, it is recommended to cut the prayer if the desire is strong, similar to the ruling on carrying a small impurity. The underlying principle is that the purpose of prayer is khushu, so anything that distracts from it is discouraged.

Key Terms
خشوع (khushu'): Focus and humility in prayer; the commentator defines it as composed of both heart (fear) and body (stillness).
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Dislike that is closer to permissible; the act is valid but better avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person begins the Maghrib prayer while dinner is served and he desires it, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but it is recommended to cut it and eat first.
C) The prayer is sinful and must be performed again after eating.
D) He should continue praying and not eat until after the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Praying while desired food is present is makruh tanzih; the prayer is valid but incomplete, and it is better to eat first to achieve khushu.

Counting Verses or Tasbih with Hand During Prayer: The Hanafi Internal Dispute
Ruling on counting verses or tasbih by hand movements during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on counting verses/tasbih with hand during prayer and apply the mufta bihi ruling in cases of necessity.

Core Idea
Finger-counting in prayer: makruh for Abu Hanifa, permissible for the Sahibayn — necessity allows the easier view.

Counting verses or tasbih during prayer is a practical concern, especially in supererogatory prayers like Salat al-Tasbih. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether moving the fingers to count is disliked. This lesson examines the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, the specific method that triggers the ruling, and how later authorities resolve the difference for the one in need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? According to Abu Hanifa, counting verses or tasbih by clenching the fingers (qabd al-asabi') during prayer is makruh. Confirm the hukm level: makruh tanzihi.
The text specifies that the disliked action is specifically 'clenching the fingers' (qabd al-asabi'), not subtle finger movements.
2
Identify the opposing view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that counting by finger movements is not makruh. Understand the basis of their disagreement: they consider such counting not a significant distraction (shughl) that detracts from khushu.
The Sahibayn's view is considered the more lenient position.
3
Analyze the distinctions between methods
The text distinguishes between: a) clenching fingers (makruh per Abu Hanifa), b) pressing fingertips in place (not makruh), c) counting by heart (permissible by consensus), d) counting by tongue (invalidates prayer by consensus). Understand why each method has a different ruling.
The restriction to 'verses and tasbih' indicates that counting other things (e.g., rakahs) is disliked by agreement.
4
Determine the mufta bihi for necessity
The commentator cites Fakhr al-Islam that the one compelled (e.g., in Salat al-Tasbih where counting is required) may follow the Sahibayn's view. Thus, in cases of need, the act is not disliked.
This is a practical concession: the easier opinion is adopted when following the stricter view would cause hardship or confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(بالقلب لا يقال القلب أشرف فينزه عن الشغل بالعد لأنا نقول شغله عند شغل الأصابع ضروري فو مشغول على كل حال فشغله فقط مع الأصابع، ولقائل أن يقول : ان شغله عند شغل الأصابع أقل منه وحده، فيكون أكثر شغله لتفهم المعاني، والتفرغ للمناجاة، فيكون أولى كما في شرح المجمع، ومن ثمة قال فخر الإسلام يعمل بقولهما في المضطر كما في سكب الأنهر. قوله: (وهي معلومة) روى أصحاب السنن عن عكرمة عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى And similarly it is disliked to count the verses (plural of ayah, which is a measured sentence from the Quran, also used for signs) and counting tasbih. And his statement 'with the hand' is a restriction for the dislike of counting verses and tasbih according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, contrary to the two (Sahibayn) by it being by clenching the fingers. And it is not disliked to press the fingertips in their place, nor counting by the heart by agreement, like counting his tasbih in the prayer of tasbih which is known. And by the tongue it invalidates by agreement. And it is not disliked outside the prayer according to the sound view. And it is disliked for the imam to stand... in meaning, as al-Kamal interpreted it; others interpreted it as when he does not desire it. His statement: 'When the evening meal of any of you is served...' and in another wording: 'When the evening meal is presented, begin with it before you pray Maghrib and do not hasten from your evening meal.' His statement: 'and due to that' meaning due to the dislike of prayer with that which disturbs the mind and detracts from khushu. His statement: 'with walking swiftly' the ba is for illustration. His statement: 'and that was not intended by the command' i.e., in His statement, the Most High: 'O you who have believed, when the call is made for prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, then proceed to the remembrance of Allah.' [Al-Jumu'ah 62:9]. His statement: 'but going' i.e., but the meaning of 'proceed' is going with tranquility and dignity. His statement: 'and similarly it is disliked to count the verses' i.e., whether one is compelled or not, and whether the prayer is obligatory or supererogatory, as narrated by Faqih Abu Ja'far. His statement: 'by being clenching the fingers' is a depiction of the disliked counting. And he only restricted it to verses and tasbih to indicate that counting other than what is mentioned is disliked by agreement, as in al-Inayah, meaning even by counting with the heart as is apparent, because it distracts from the purpose. His statement: 'and not' counting with the heart; it is not said that the heart is nobler so it is free from occupation with counting, because we say: his occupation when the fingers are occupied is necessary, so he is occupied in any case. So his occupation only with the fingers is more than by itself? And it is possible to say that his occupation when the fingers are occupied is less than by itself? And [the commentary continues with discussion on salat al-tasbih].
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage rules on counting verses of the Quran or tasbih with the hand during prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, it is makruh to count by clenching the fingers (i.e., physically moving the fingers to keep count). However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that it is not makruh, except when done consciously? The commentator explains that the disliked act is specifically counting by hand movements; counting by pressing the fingertips in one place (without obvious movement) is not disliked, and counting silently in the heart is permissible by consensus. Counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer. Outside of prayer, it is not disliked. There is also a mention of the imam standing? But the text then shifts to a long hadith about salat al-tasbih, which is given as an example of a recommended prayer where counting with the heart is allowed. The commentator notes that in cases of necessity (e.g., someone who must count tasbih to complete the prayer correctly), the view of the Sahibayn is followed, as stated by Fakhr al-Islam. The discussion reflects the Hanafi internal dispute: Abu Hanifa sees hand movements as a distraction while the Sahibayn see no issue if done discretely.

Key Terms
الآي (al-ayi): Verses of the Quran; the commentator defines it as complete sentences from the Quran, but also can mean signs.
قبض الأصابع (qabd al-asabi'): Clenching the fingers; the action of moving fingers to count, which is considered makruh.
غمز بالأنامل (ghamz bi al-anamil): Pressing with the fingertips in place without moving them; not disliked.
الإحصاء بالقلب (al-ihsa' bil qalb): Counting by the heart (silently); permissible by consensus.
صلاة التسبيح (Salat al-Tasbih): A supererogatory prayer that includes 75 tasbih in each rak'ah; an example where counting is needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi position for the one compelled, what is the ruling on counting verses by clenching the fingers during prayer?
A) It is absolutely forbidden and invalidates the prayer.
B) It is disliked but the prayer remains valid.
C) It is permissible and not disliked.
D) It is recommended to aid concentration.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, counting with hand during prayer is an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa considers it makruh, but for the one compelled, the Sahibayn's permissive view is followed.

Images and Row Gaps in Prayer
Ruling on images and row gaps in prayer with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images of living beings in prayer and identify the exceptions (small, headless, non-living) that remove the dislike.

Core Idea
Images of living beings in prayer are disliked because they resemble idolatry, but small or headless images are excepted.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies two related elements of prayer: the virtue of closing gaps in rows and the dislike of images of living beings. The author explains the degrees of dislike and the exceptions based on size and form, helping us apply the ruling correctly in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage deals with two acts: wearing a garment with an image of a living being (disliked) and having an image in front, behind, above, or beside the worshipper (disliked). The ruling for the latter is further detailed by direction and exceptions.
The overall hukm is makruh tahrimi.
2
Understand the hadith on closing gaps
The passage begins by citing a hadith that promises reward for closing gaps in rows. This serves as a motivation to maintain straight and connected rows, which is a sunnah muakkadah.
The hadith is cited as dalil for the virtue, not for the prohibition of images.
3
Analyze the ruling on images
The text states that having an image of a living being (animal or human) in front, behind, above, or beside the worshipper is disliked. The most severe dislike is for images in front, then above, then right, then left, then behind.
The reasoning: it resembles worshipping the image (shirk).
4
Note the exceptions
Three exceptions remove the dislike: (1) the image is small enough that it is not noticeable without careful contemplation (like on a dinar), (2) the image is large but the head is cut off, (3) the image is of a non-living thing (e.g., a tree).
The key is that the image could be worshipped; small or headless images are not typically worshipped.
5
Apply the exception conditions
If you have a coin with a small figure, or a picture of a tree, or a large picture with no head, the prayer is not disliked. The passage also mentions that erasing an image seen in another's house is permissible (and recommended).
Cutting the head removes the soul-like aspect, so it is no longer an image of a living being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرجات الشيطان، ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من سد فرجة من الصف كتب له عشر حسنات ومحي عنه عشر سيات ورفع له عشر درجات ولبس ثوب فيه تصاوير ذي روح لأنه يشبه حامل الصنم (و) يكره أن يكون فوق رأسه أو خلفه، أو بين يديه أو بحذائه (صورة) حيوان لأنه يشبه عبادتها وأشدها كراهة أمامه، ثم فوقه ثم يمينه ثم يساره ثم خلفه ألا أن تكون صغيرة) بحيث لا تبدو للقائم إلا بتأمل كالتي على الدينار لأنها لا تعبد عادة ولو صلى ومعه دراهم عليها تماثيل ملك لا بأس به لأن هذا يصغر عن البصر (أو) تكون كبيرة (مقطوعة الرأس) لأنها لا تعبد بلا رأس (أو) تكون لغير ذي (روح) كالشجر لأنها لا تعبد، وإذا رأى صورة في بيت غيره يجوز له محوها وتغييرها
The gaps of Satan, and for his saying peace be upon him: Whoever closes a gap in the row, ten good deeds are written for him, ten misdeeds are erased, and ten degrees are raised. And wearing a garment with images of a living being is disliked because it resembles the carrier of an idol. And it is disliked that above his head, behind him, in front of him, or beside him be an image of an animal because it resembles worshipping it. The most severely disliked is in front, then above, then right, then left, then behind, unless it is small so that it does not appear to the one standing except with contemplation, like that on a dinar, because it is not usually worshipped. And if he prays with dirhams on which are figures of a king, there is no harm because this is too small for the eye. Or it is large but cut off at the head, because it is not worshipped without a head. Or it is of something without a soul, like a tree, because it is not worshipped. And if he sees an image in someone else's house, it is permissible for him to erase it and change it.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya rules on disliked elements in prayer, focusing on images and row organization. It begins by stating the virtue of closing gaps in rows, citing a hadith about reward. Then it addresses wearing clothes with images of living beings, explaining that it resembles idol-carriers and is thus disliked. The ruling extends to having images of animals in front, behind, above, or beside the worshipper, with the strongest dislike for images in front. Exceptions are given for small images (like on dinars) that are not normally worshipped, for large images with the head cut off (since they cannot be worshipped), and for images of non-living things like trees. Finally, it permits erasing images seen in another's house, implying an obligation to remove them if possible. The commentary also discusses nuances: images on coins or rings that are not discernible are not disliked, and cutting the head removes dislike only if the image is rendered non-living. The tone is explanatory, clarifying the reasons (resemblance to idolatry) and degrees of dislike.

Key Terms
صورة (surah): An image or picture, specifically of a living being (animal or human).
صنم (sanam): An idol, specifically a statue of a human form made from wood, gold, or silver.
وثن (wathan): An idol made of stone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following removes the dislike of an image in prayer?
A) The image is of an animal without a tail.
B) The image is large but the head is cut off.
C) The image is placed behind the worshipper.
D) The image is in color.

Key Takeaway
Praying with images of living beings is disliked but not invalid; small, headless, or non-living images are excepted.

Makruh Acts: Fire, Sleepers, and Specifying Surahs
Detailing disliked acts: fire in front, sleeping people, wiping forehead, and specifying surahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four disliked acts in prayer (oven/brazier, sleeping people, wiping forehead, specifying a surah) and explain the conditions that make each permissible or not.

Core Idea
A disliked act in prayer may become permissible when the reason for dislike is removed or when one follows Prophetic practice.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi clarifies several acts that are considered makruh tanzihi during prayer, but with important caveats. The rulings are not absolute; they depend on context, such as the type of object, the risk of harm, or the intention behind the action. By understanding these nuances, you will be able to distinguish when an act is genuinely disliked and when it is permissible or even recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify each disliked act
List the four acts mentioned: having an oven/brazier with embers in front, having sleeping people in front, wiping dust from the forehead, and specifying a particular surah (other than al-Fatihah).
Each is ruled makruh tanzihi in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the reason for dislike
For each act, note why it is disliked. Oven/brazier resembles Magian fire worship; sleeping people risk embarrassment; wiping dust is playfulness; specifying a surah abandons other surahs.
3
Note the exceptions
Identify when the dislike is lifted: other items like lamps are not disliked; sleeping people if no fear; wiping dust if harmful; specifying surah if done for ease or to follow Prophet's practice.
The exceptions are supported by hadith.
4
Recognize the evidence
For sleeping people, Aisha's hadith shows the Prophet prayed while she slept in front. For specifying surahs, multiple hadiths show the Prophet recited specific surahs on occasion, making it recommended to follow.
The dalil is ahad but sufficient for the ruling.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Use the principles to evaluate similar cases, e.g., electric heater vs. brazier, habitual recitation vs. Prophetic practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره أن يكون بين يديه (أي المصلي) تنور أو كانون فيه جمر لأنه يشبه المجوس في حال عبادتهم لها لا شمع وقنديل، وسراج في الصحيح لأنه لا يشبه التعبد (أو) يكون بين يديه (قوم) نيام يخشى خروج ما يضحك أو يخجل، أو يؤذي أو يقابل وجهاً وإلا فلا كراهة لأنّ عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي صلاة الليل كلها وأنا معترضة بينه وبين القبلة، فإذا أراد أن يوتر أيقظني فأوتر (و) يكره (مسح الجبهة من تراب لا يضره في خلال الصلاة) لأنه نوع عبث وإذا ضره لا بأس به في الصلاة وبعد الفراغ، وكذا مسح العرق (و) يكره (تعيين سورة) غير الفاتحة لأنها متعينة وجوباً وكذا المسنون المعين وهذا بحيث لا يقرأ غيرها) لما فيه من هجر الباقي (إلا) ليسر عليه أو تبركاً بقراءة النبي ) فلا يكره، ويستحب اقتداؤه بقراءة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كالسجدة ، وهل أتى بفجر الجمعة أحياناً، وقد ذكرنا في الأصل جملة من السور التي قرأ بها النبي المسندة وهذه أصولها، فما جاء في الصحيح كان يقرأ في الصبح بيس كان يقر في الصبح بالواقعة، ونحوها من السور قرأ في الصبح بسورة الروم كان في سفر فصلي الغداة فقرأ فيها قل أعوذ برب الفلق، وقل أعوذ برب الناس صلى الفجر بأقصر بهم سورتين من القرآن وأوجز فلما قضى الصلاة قال له معاذ يا رسول الله صليت صلاة ما صليت مثلها قط قال : أما سمعت بكاء الصبي خلفي في صف النساء أردت أن أفرغ له أمه قرأ في الصبح إذا زلزلت صلى الصبح بمكة، فاستفتح سورة المؤمنين حتى جاء ذكر هرون وموسى
And it is disliked that in front of him (i.e., the worshipper) be an oven or a brazier with embers, because it resembles the Magians in their act of worshipping it. Not wax, a lamp, or a lantern, in the correct view, because they do not resemble worship. Or that in front of him be sleeping people, fearing emission that causes laughter, shame, harm, or that he faces a face; otherwise there is no dislike, because Aisha (may God be pleased with her) said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) used to pray all of the night prayer while I was lying between him and the qibla. When he wanted to pray witr, he would wake me and pray witr. And it is disliked to wipe the forehead from dust that does not harm him during the prayer, because it is a kind of play. But if it harms him, there is no harm in doing it during prayer and after finishing. Similarly, wiping sweat. And it is disliked to specify a surah other than al-Fatihah, because it is obligatory to be specific, and similarly the specified sunnah, such that he does not recite other than it, because it involves abandoning the rest, unless it is easier for him or as a blessing by following the recitation of the Prophet, then it is not disliked. And it is recommended to follow the Prophet's recitation, like the surah of prostration, and 'Hal ata' on Friday Fajr sometimes. And we have mentioned in the original a number of surahs that the Prophet recited with chain, and here are their essences. Among what is authentic: He used to recite in Fajr: Ya Sin. He used to recite in Fajr: al-Waqi'ah and similar surahs. He recited in Fajr: Surat al-Rum. He was on a journey and prayed the morning prayer and recited in it: 'Qul a'udhu bi rabb al-falaq' and 'Qul a'udhu bi rabb al-nas'. He prayed Fajr with the two shortest surahs of the Quran and shortened, and when he finished the prayer, Mu'adh said to him: O Messenger of God, you prayed a prayer you have never prayed before. He said: Did you not hear the boy crying behind me in the women's row? I wanted to free his mother for him. He recited in Fajr: 'Idha zulzilat'. He prayed Fajr in Mecca and started Surat al-Mu'minun until mention of Harun and Musa.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of disliked acts in prayer. First, having an oven or brazier with embers in front is disliked because it resembles Zoroastrian fire worship, but a wax candle, lamp, or lantern is not disliked as they have no such resemblance. Second, having sleeping people in front is disliked if one fears involuntary emission that could cause embarrassment or harm; otherwise, there is no dislike, as shown by Aisha's hadith of sleeping in front of the Prophet during his night prayer. Third, wiping dust from the forehead during prayer is disliked if it does not cause discomfort, being a form of playing; if it causes harm, it is permissible. Fourth, specifying a particular surah (other than al-Fatihah) for recitation is disliked if one limits oneself to it, abandoning others, unless it is easier or to follow the Prophet's example. The text then provides a list of surahs the Prophet recited in Fajr prayer, showing that following his practice is recommended and not disliked. The commentary explains that the list includes surahs like Ya Sin, al-Waqi'ah, al-Rum, al-Falaq, al-Nas, al-Zalzalah, and al-Mu'minun, often recited in both rak'ahs. It notes that specifying a surah is only disliked if one believes the prayer is invalid without it, but without such belief, it is not disliked. The mention of 'sometimes' indicates that continuous practice of a specific surah is disliked, while occasional recitation for ease or blessing is encouraged.

Key Terms
تنور (tannur): An oven, specifically a type of clay oven used for baking.
كانون (kanun): A brazier or fire-pan used for holding embers or coals.
تعيين سورة (ta'yin surat): The act of specifying a particular surah to recite in prayer (other than al-Fatihah) to the exclusion of others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is specifying a single surah for recitation in prayer not disliked?
A) When the surah is al-Fatihah.
B) When one does so to follow the Prophet's recitation as a blessing.
C) When the surah is short.
D) When one recites it silently.

Key Takeaway
Disliked acts in prayer are context-dependent; they are not absolute but lift with necessity, absence of harm, or following Prophetic practice.

Disliked Actions in Prayer: Fire, Sleepers, Dust, and Specifying a Surah
Refines rulings on four disliked actions in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify four disliked actions in Hanafi fiqh, state the reasons and conditions for each, and apply exceptions correctly.

Core Idea
Actions resembling worship of fire, risking disturbance, fidgeting, or neglecting other surahs are disliked in prayer.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya clarifies several disliked actions in prayer, offering both the underlying rationale and the conditions under which the dislike is lifted. Understanding these nuances helps the worshipper maintain proper etiquette and avoid subtle violations while preserving the validity and reward of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four disliked actions
Read the source text and list all four actions ruled as disliked (makruh) in prayer: facing fire, praying while people are sleeping in front, wiping dust/sweat from the forehead, and specifying a surah other than al-Fatiha.
These are distinct rulings, each with its own condition and proof.
2
Understand the rationale for each
For each action, determine the legal cause (illah): imitation of Magians, fear of disturbance, fidgeting (abath), and neglect of other surahs.
The rationale shapes the scope of the ruling.
3
Note the conditions that lift the dislike
Examine when the dislike disappears: for fire, if it is a candle/lamp (no resemblance); for sleepers, if there is no fear of disturbance (based on the hadith); for wiping, if it is harmful to leave it; for specifying a surah, if done occasionally for ease or blessing.
These exceptions show that the default ruling is contextual.
4
Analyze the proof for the sleeping people case
Study the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet prayed while she lay across his qibla, establishing that no dislike exists if there is no fear of disturbance. The opposite case (fear) is disliked by implication.
This is a clear example of dalil naqli (hadith) used to derive a ruling.
5
Synthesize the ruling on specifying a surah
Combine the general rule (dislike if leads to neglect or belief of obligation) with the exceptions (occasional recitation for emulating the Prophet). Note that specifying a sunnah surah (e.g., in witr) is not disliked.
This shows the Hanafi method of balancing primary and secondary considerations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنور أو كانون فيه جمر لأنه يشبه المجوس في حال عبادتهم لها لا شمع وقنديل، وسراج في الصحيح لأنه لا يشبه التعبد (أو) يكون بين يديه (قوم) نيام يخشى خروج ما يضحك أو يخجل، أو يؤذي أو يقابل وجهاً وإلا فلا كراهة لأنّ عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي صلاة الليل كلها وأنا معترضة بينه وبين القبلة، فإذا أراد أن يوتر أيقظني فأوتر (و) يكره (مسح الجبهة من تراب لا يضره في خلال الصلاة) لأنه نوع عبث وإذا ضره لا بأس به في الصلاة وبعد الفراغ، وكذا مسح العرق (و) يكره (تعيين سورة) غير الفاتحة لأنها متعينة وجوباً وكذا المسنون المعين وهذا بحيث لا يقرأ غيرها) لما فيه من هجر الباقي (إلا) ليسر عليه أو تبركاً بقراءة النبي ) فلا يكره، ويستحب اقتداؤه بقراءة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كالسجدة ، وهل أتى بفجر الجمعة أحياناً،

( قوله : (يجوز له محوها) أن قال السيد وينبغي يجب عليه ولو استأجر مصوراً فلا أجر له لأن عمله معصية، ولو هدم بيتاً فيه تصاوير ضمن قيمته خالياً عنها اهـ . قوله : (لا شمع الخ) في فتاوى الحجة الأولى ترك ذلك قال الحلبي وكأنه لما فيه من الجزئية، وفي النهر عن البحر ينبغي أن الشمع لو كان إلى جانبه كما يفعل في المساجد ليالي رمضان لا كراهة اتفاقاً . قوله : (أو يكون بين يديه قوم نيام) الظاهر أن الشخص الواحد عند وجود ما ذكر كذلك، ويحرر . قوله : ( فأوتر) بضم الهمزة، وضميره إلى عائشة قوله : (ويكره تعيين سورة قيد الطحاوي الكراهة بما إذا اعتقد أن الصلاة لا تجوز بغيرها أما إذا لم يعتقد ذلك فلا كراهة أفاده في الشرح قوله : (وكذا المستون المعين) كقراءة سور الوتر. قوله : (أحياناً) يفيد كراهة المداومة.
A tandoor or kanun containing embers [is disliked] because it resembles the Magians in their worship of fire, not a candle, oil lamp, or lantern in the correct view because it does not resemble worship. Or [if] there are sleeping people in front of him, fearing that something that causes laughter or embarrassment or annoyance might come out, or if he faces a face; otherwise there is no dislike because Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to pray the night prayer while I lay between him and the qibla, and when he wanted to pray witr he would wake me and I would pray witr.' And it is disliked to wipe the forehead from dust that does not harm him during prayer because it is a form of fidgeting; if it harms him there is no harm in doing it during prayer or after finishing; similarly wiping sweat. And it is disliked to specify a surah other than al-Fatiha because it is obligatory, and also the specified sunnah, such that he does not read other than it, because that involves abandoning the rest, except for ease or seeking blessing from the Prophet's recitation, then it is not disliked. And it is recommended to follow the Prophet's recitation, like Surat as-Sajdah and Hal Ata, occasionally on Friday at Fajr.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from the hashya, addressing several disliked actions (makruhat) in prayer. First, it is disliked to pray facing an oven or brazier with live embers because it imitates the Magians' fire-worship; this does not apply to candles, oil lamps, or lanterns. Second, if there are sleeping people in front, there is fear of disturbing them, hence dislike; the proof is the hadith of Aisha where she lay across the Prophet's prayer direction and he did not object, showing no dislike in that case because it was not the same situation. Third, wiping dust or sweat from the forehead during prayer is disliked as fidgeting, unless it causes harm. Fourth, specifying a particular surah besides Fatiha is disliked if one believes prayer is invalid without it, or if one consistently neglects other surahs; but if done occasionally for ease or to emulate the Prophet's practice, it is recommended. The footnotes clarify that the specification is only disliked when accompanied by a mistaken belief of obligation or constant neglect; the Prophet's occasional recitation of specific surahs is a recommended practice.

Key Terms
تعيين سورة (ta'yin surat): Specifying a particular surah to recite in prayer, excluding others.
مسنون معين (masnun mu'ayyan): A specified sunnah surah, like the witr surahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked to pray facing a tandoor with fire?
A) Because it resembles the worship of fire by Magians
B) Because it causes distraction
C) Because it is considered najis
D) Because it invalidates prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between absolute dislike and contextual dislike, lifting the ruling when the underlying cause is absent or when necessity or prophetic practice dictates.

The Prophet's Recitation Sunnah in Daily Prayers
Compilation of hadith on recitation patterns

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sunnah recitation in prayer and identify the surahs recommended for each prayer based on the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Prophet's recitation varied; following his example is sunnah muakkadah, but any valid Quran recitation suffices.

This passage compiles authentic reports of the Prophet's recitation in the five daily prayers, showing a consistent yet flexible practice. The Hanafi school treats this as a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) — emulating the Prophet is meritorious, but not obligatory. Al-Tahtawi's commentary refines the understanding by noting the chains are omitted for brevity and that the Prophet occasionally varied his recitation for reasons like accommodating a child's cry.

Guided Path
1
Identify each prayer and its associated surahs
Go through the passage and list the surahs mentioned for Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. Note that some reports give specific surahs, others give general categories like 'from al-Mufassal'.
E.g., Fajr: Ya Sin, al-Waqi'a, ar-Rum, al-Mu'awwidhatan, idha Zulzilat, Qaf, etc.
2
Recognise the pattern of length
The Prophet recited longer surahs in Fajr (e.g., 20+ verses), medium-length in Zuhr and Asr, shorter in Maghrib, and variable in Isha. This pattern is sunnah.
The commentator notes the minimum for Fajr is 20 verses, for Isha 10 verses.
3
Determine the ruling level
The Hanafi position is that this recitation is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not fard or wajib. The variety in the reports shows flexibility.
The passage does not use the term 'sunnah muakkadah' explicitly, but the later Hanafi authorities classify it as such.
4
Understand the scope of flexibility
The Prophet sometimes changed recitation for a reason (e.g., hearing a child cry). This indicates that while following the sunnah is recommended, the prayer remains valid with any surah.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is: follow the sunnah when possible, but any valid recitation is acceptable.
5
Apply the principle to practice
When praying, especially as an imam, one may vary recitation. For personal prayer, choose surahs from the sunnah patterns. But reciting any part of the Quran fulfils the obligation of qira'ah.
The prayer is valid even if one recites only al-Fatiha, but adding a surah is sunnah.

We have mentioned in the original (matn) a number of surahs that the Prophet recited, with their chains; these are their texts. Among what is authentic: He used to recite in Fajr Surah Ya Sin, Surah al-Waqi'a, and similar surahs. He recited in Fajr Surah ar-Rum when traveling; he prayed Fajr and recited 'Qul A'udhu bi-Rabb al-Falaq' and 'Qul A'udhu bi-Rabb an-Nas'. He prayed Fajr with the two shortest surahs from the Quran and was brief; when he finished, Mu'adh said: O Messenger of Allah, you prayed a prayer like never before. He said: Did you not hear the crying of a child behind me in the women's row? I wanted to free his mother. He recited in Fajr 'Idha Zulzilat'. He prayed Fajr in Makkah and began Surah al-Mu'minun until the mention of Harun and Musa came, then he bowed. He used to recite in Fajr 'Qaf' and 'al-Qur'an al-Majid'. He said: Do not recite in Fajr less than twenty verses, and do not recite in Isha less than ten verses. Among what came for Zuhr and Asr: He used to recite in Zuhr 'Wa al-Layli idha Yaghsha', and in Asr similar, and in Fajr longer than that. He recited in Fajr 'Subh Isma Rabbika al-A'la', and in Zuhr longer than that. He recited in Zuhr and Asr 'Wa as-Samai dhat al-Buruj' and 'Wa as-Samai wa at-Tariq' and similar surahs. He led us in Zuhr and we heard him recite verse after verse from Surah Luqman and adh-Dhariyat. He prayed Zuhr and prostrated, so we thought he recited 'Tanzeel as-Sajdah'. He used to recite in Zuhr and Asr 'Subh Isma Rabbika al-A'la' and 'Hal Ataka Hadith al-Ghashiya'. He led them in Zuhr and raised his voice reciting 'Wa ash-Shamsi wa Duhaha' and 'Wa al-Layli idha Yaghsha'. Ubayy ibn Ka'b said: O Messenger of Allah, were you commanded something in this prayer? He said: No, but I wanted to teach you the timing. Among what came for Maghrib: It is authentic that he recited in Maghrib Surah al-A'raf, Surah al-Anfal, and 'Alladheena Kafaru wa Saddu 'An Sabeelillah'. The last prayer the Prophet prayed was Maghrib; in the first rak'ah he recited 'Subh Isma Rabbika al-A'la', in the second 'Qul Ya Ayyuha al-Kafirun'. He recited in Maghrib 'at-Teen wa az-Zaytun', 'Ha Meem', and 'al-Qari'a'. He used to recite in Maghrib on Friday night 'Qul Ya Ayyuha al-Kafirun' and 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad'. He used to recite in Isha on Friday night Surah al-Jumu'ah and al-Munafiqun. And in Isha: 'at-Teen wa az-Zaytun'. Ibn Umar said: There is no surah, small or large, from al-Mufassal but I heard the Prophet recite it in the obligatory prayer. End of what we have transmitted from al-Jalal al-Suyuti (may Allah have mercy on him) to be emulated.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement presenting a collection of hadith on the Prophet's recitation patterns in the five daily prayers. The commentator explains that the original text (matn) mentioned these surahs with their chains, but here only the texts are given. The purpose is to show the recommended (sunnah) practice. For Fajr, the Prophet often recited longer surahs like Ya Sin, al-Waqi'a, or shorter ones like al-Mu'awwidhatan on occasion, and he set a minimum of twenty verses. For Zuhr and Asr, he recited medium-length surahs like al-Layl, al-Buruj, and at-Tariq, sometimes longer like Luqman. For Maghrib, he recited shorter surahs like al-Kafirun, al-Ikhlas, or occasionally longer ones like al-A'raf. For Isha, he recited surahs like at-Teen and al-Mufassal. The footnotes clarify details: 'مسندة' means with chain; the two shortest surahs in this context are the Mu'awwidhatan, not al-Asr or al-Kawthar; the recitation in Maghrib of 'at-Teen' might be split across rak'ahs or repeated. The commentator emphasizes that following the Prophet's recitation is recommended (mustahabb).

Key Terms
مسندة (musnada): Hadith with a full chain of transmission (sanad) mentioned.
المفصل (al-mufassal): The surahs from Qaf or al-Hujurat to the end of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of verses recommended for Fajr prayer according to the hadith?
A) 10 verses
B) 20 verses
C) 30 verses
D) No minimum

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's recitation in prayer is a sunnah to be emulated, but flexibility is allowed, and any valid Quran recitation fulfills the obligation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Minimum Recitation Lengths in Daily Prayers: Ruling of Karaha Tanzihiyyah
Hadith proofs and hashya ruling on minimal recitation per prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on minimal Quran recitation in each prayer and identify the legal status (makruh tanzih) when reciting less than the prescribed amounts.

Core Idea
Reciting less than twenty verses in Fajr or ten in Isha is makruh tanzih—disliked but not sinful.

This lesson examines a passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi that compiles numerous hadith on the Prophet's recitation lengths in the five daily prayers. The hashya clarifies that the prohibition against reciting less than the mentioned amounts is for tanzih (disliked), not tahrim (prohibited), because it involves abandoning a confirmed sunnah. Understanding this ruling helps avoid undue strictness while preserving the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting Quran in the obligatory prayers. The ruling is that reciting less than the minimum amounts (20 verses in Fajr, 10 in Isha, etc.) is makruh tanzih.
The hashya explicitly states: 'al-nahy li al-tanzih'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proofs are multiple hadith narrations quoted from Jalal al-Suyuti, showing the Prophet's practice in each prayer.
The hadith are used as evidence for the sunnah amounts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hashya interprets the prohibition (nahy) in the hadith as indicating dislike (karaha) rather than prohibition (haram), because it is in contrast to leaving the sunnah.
The operative phrase is 'al-nahy li al-tanzih'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may consider these amounts as mustahab or even wajib. The Hanafi position is clearly makruh tanzih.
Cross-madhhab difference: e.g., Shafi'is may view it as sunnah, not makruh.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) is that reciting less is makruh tanzih, as confirmed by later Hanafi authorities like al-Tahtawi.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Book of Prayer. And Musa bowed - He used to recite in Fajr 'Qaf and the Glorious Quran.' He said: Do not recite in Fajr without twenty verses, nor in Isha without ten verses. And what has come regarding Zuhr and Asr: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to recite in Zuhr 'By the night when it covers', and in Asr similarly, and in Fajr longer than that. And regarding Maghrib: It is authentically reported that the Prophet recited in Maghrib 'Al-A'raf'. He used to recite in Maghrib Surah Al-Anfal. He used to recite for them in Maghrib 'Those who disbelieved and averted [others] from the way of Allah'. The last prayer the Messenger of Allah ﷺ prayed was Maghrib; he recited in the first rak'ah 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High' and in the second 'Say, O disbelievers'. He recited in Maghrib 'By the fig and the olive'. He recited in Maghrib 'Ha Meem'. He prayed Maghrib and recited 'Al-Qari'ah'. He used to recite in Maghrib on the night of Friday 'Say, O disbelievers' and 'Say, He is Allah, [the] One'. And he used to recite in Isha on the night of Friday Surah Al-Jumu'ah and Al-Munafiqun. And regarding Isha: From this recent [narration] - from Jubayr bin Mut'im: I heard the Prophet ﷺ recite in Isha 'By the fig and the olive'. From Abu Rafi': I prayed Isha with Abu Hurayrah and he recited 'When the sky is split open' and prostrated, so I asked him, and he said: I prostrated behind Abu al-Qasim. The Prophet ﷺ used to recite in Isha 'By the sky containing great stars' and 'By the sky and the night-comer'. He used to command lightness and would lead us with 'As-Saffat'. From Ibn Umar: There is no surah small or large from Al-Mufassal except that I heard the Prophet ﷺ recite it with the people in the obligatory prayer. End of what we have transmitted from Jalal al-Suyuti (may Allah have mercy on him) so that whoever preserves what has reached him of the noble Sunnah may act accordingly. And you have known the details of recitation from Al-Mufassal in the times according to us. And Allah is the Grantor of success. His saying: (until the mention of Harun and Musa) or the mention of Isa, then the Prophet ﷺ was seized by a cough and bowed. His saying: (Do not recite in Fajr) the prohibition is for tanzih because it is in the face of abandoning the Sunnah. His saying: (masjid) i.e., for recitation. His saying: (al-hajirah) it is Zuhr prayer. His saying: (and the night when it covers) i.e., in the second rak'ah. His saying: (Have you been commanded something in this prayer?) i.e., which is the loud recitation. His saying: (that I might set a time for you) i.e., I estimated for you the amount of recitation in it. His saying: (this recent) i.e., Surah Al-Jumu'ah and Al-Munafiqun. His saying: (He used to recite in Isha with at-Tin) it is possible that he divided it and possible that he repeated it. His saying: (al-atamah) i.e., Isha. His saying: (So I said to him) i.e., questioning about the reason. His saying: (in the obligatory prayer) includes the five prayers. His saying: (from Jalal al-Suyuti) mentioned it in his book called Al-Yanbu'.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadith narrations regarding the Prophet's recitation in the five daily prayers, quoted by the hashya author from Jalal al-Suyuti's work. The hashya then provides brief linguistic and legal clarifications. The core ruling derived here is that it is makruh tanzih (disliked, not prohibited) to recite fewer than twenty verses in Fajr and fewer than ten verses in Isha. The hashya explicitly states that the prohibition is for tanzih because reducing recitation below the prophetic practice abandons a sunnah. The passages also indicate the general lengths for Zuhr and Asr (medium-length surahs), and for Maghrib (short surahs of Mufassal). The hashya also clarifies that the term 'masjid' here means 'for recitation' (i.e., the place of prostration in the Quran). The overall purpose is to guide the reader on the proper amounts of Quran recitation in each prayer, based on the Sunnah, and to indicate that while it is not sinful to recite less, it is disliked.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karaha tanzihiyyah): A legal status meaning disliked but not sinful; omitting the sunnah but not incurring punishment.
مفصل (mufassal): The section of the Quran from Surah Qaf to the end, consisting of shorter surahs often recited in prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on reciting less than twenty verses in Fajr prayer?
A) It invalidates the prayer
B) It is makruh tanzih
C) It is wajib to repeat
D) It is makruh tahrimi

Key Takeaway
Reciting less than the prophetic amounts (20 in Fajr, 10 in Isha, medium in Zuhr/Asr, short in Maghrib) is makruh tanzih, not haram.
